Oh, sons, now I have completed this book for you, which is the final part of the science of medicine, since its completion has brought it to an end, and through its explanations and declarations, it is my wish that you may learn from this treatise, which is a part of surgery, carried out by myself.
For the surgery done by me is spread out in our region and in our time, and it has been utterly privatized; so that the science of it is greatly endangered, and its practice is obstructed; and there remain only a few small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which have been altered more and corrupted into those errors and mistakes, until the intentions of it are closed off and the force of it and the art are exhausted.
And it is clear to me that you must revitalize that ancient order of this treatise through the method of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and so that the forms of the instruments of cautery and other tools of the work may be added to the declaration, and prepared for use, which necessity arises.
But the reason why a good craftsman cannot be found with his own hand in our present time is that the art of medicine is long and requires its actor to have been exercised beforehand in the science of anatomy, which was understood by Galen, so that he knows the joints of the members and their forms, and their conjunction and separation; and has knowledge of the bones, nerves, and ligaments, and their number and arrangement; and also of the pulsating veins and quiet ones, and the locations of their effusion.
And therefore says Hippocrates that a name is not enough, but rather in small work and most of all in the art of one's hand.
But we have already said this about him in the introduction to this book; for whoever is not well-versed in anatomy as we have described it, will not be spared from falling into error by which many men are killed, just as I have seen many of those who are thus formed in this science and take themselves out of that without science or experience.
For you saw a foolish and inexperienced doctor who had caused an abscess to form in the throat of a woman, and had cut some arteries in the throat so that a great deal of blood flowed, and as a result the woman died between them.
And you saw another doctor who ordered that a stone be removed from a man's bladder, which had progressed in his condition, and the stone was large, and he came to him and removed that stone with a piece of his own intestines, so that that man died on the third day.
And you yourself had already appealed to remove it, and saw that due to the largeness of the stone and the condition of the patient, one could conclude above him that he would die.
And you saw another doctor who took payment from the duke of our land for surgery, and endeavored to set the fracture of a blacksmith's broken leg; but the doctor prepared it with his ignorance, removed the fracture above the wound with pulleys and astels with great tension, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
And then he loosened it according to his desires, and then relaxed the bandage, and then loosened it again after some days and commanded us to loosen the bond; and thus it was that the leg and foot became gangrened, and came to destruction.
And you were called to him, and I prepared to loosen the bond, and as a result he obtained relief and began to be freed from his pains.
But meanwhile corruption had already been confirmed in the member, so that it could not be restrained, and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the patient was in mortal danger.
And you saw another doctor who pierced a cancerous abscess and allowed it to ulcerate about three days later, until the great majesty of the disease overpowered his lordship.
Which is because the melancholic humor is pure in the cancerous person, whereas it does not need to be brought forth by iron, but rather to be present in a member that suffers from being completely possessed.
And therefore, sons, it is necessary for you that the operation done by me be divided into two parts: one is in the operation which is associated with health, and the other is in the work where there is danger to the greater dispositions.
And you have already existed in this place throughout this book where the operation is one of error and fear; therefore it is necessary for you to keep this in mind and avoid that, so that foolish people do not get in the way of speaking and dishonestly besmirching your reputation.
And therefore, take up your own arms with solicitude and the protection of God, and your patients with felicity and firmness.
And use the best method through the grace of God to achieve salvation and glorious success, and overcome terrifying illnesses that are difficult to heal, and stand your ground with these arms that make you afraid, so that your position in your faith and in your name does not fail: for it is more remaining to your glory, and even more in this world and in the end to your sanctity.
Galen has said so in some of his own monodies: "'Do not heal bad illnesses, lest you be called a bad doctor'".
And I have divided this book into three chapters.
The division of the book begins, and the first part of the first chapter. The first chapter, orderly arranged from head to foot, in the forms of instruments and iron tools for cauterization, and of what is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, on dryness and perforation, and on cupping glasses, wounds, and extraction of splinters and similar things, all chaptered and ordered in the forms of instruments.
The third chapter, on restoration and dislocation, and on curing of twists and similar things; chapter ordered from head to foot, and of the forms of instruments.
You must say what quality the joints of that cautery have, and what are its defects, and in what condition it is prohibited to use cautery.
Therefore I say that the sermon on the quality of the joint of cautery and its defects is a long and prolix one, subtle in science, and hidden in secret; and many wise men have spoken about it, and they have disagreed among themselves, and to me it seems sufficient to present a small part of their sermons, fearing prolivity.
And therefore I say that cautery is suitable for all general conditions universally, which are in matter or of matter, except two conditions, which are hot humoral conditions.
In the hot and dry condition with matter, it dries out; for some say that cautery is beneficial for this, while others say the opposite, that cautery is not suitable in a disease which is due to quality and dryness, because the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and it is inconvenient that a hot and dry disease, with water that is hot and dry, should be cured.
And say that which says the opposite of this, that through cautery, the joint is made in all hot and dry diseases that are found in the bodies of men, for when you compare the body of man and its humors to the condition of fire, you find the body of man cold.
And I say by the sermon of that, that this experiment has already been discovered to me on several occasions.
But it is not necessary that this come to light again about what has already been experimented and exercised in the chapter of cautery, and to understand the diversity of human conditions and the disposition of diseases in their respective members, and the causes of those, and the accidents of theirs, and the space of time for those.
But in other conditions, there is no fear for you, and most especially in cold and humid diseases, for all doctors have agreed on those, and are not discordant about the joint of cautery in those.
And know, sons, that from the secret of healing through cautery with fire and its goodness, it is clear that those who use cautery with medicine are in error, for fire is simple, and its action only reaches the member being cauterized, not affecting another member connected to it except with slight harm.
But the action of medicine combined reaches that member which is distant from it, and easily brings disease to a difficult-to-cure member, and easily causes harm.
But fire, because of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do this except that it superfluously adds. And already we have known through experiment and long service in studying the art, on the truth of causes; and therefore I am excused from the length of the sermon. But if it were not for the fact that it is not read in a better book in this pause, to you, a secret hidden in fire, and the quality of the operation of it in bodies, and its expulsion by which it expels diseases, with a philosophical demonstration, which would be suitable for your souls.
And know, sons, that they disagree on the time in which it is convenient to do cautery and pause at the best time of spring.
And I say that cautery is convenient at any time, for the damage caused by the accidental time is submerged in the joint of this which is attracted to the cautery, and most especially if the cautery is for pains or necessary pains, strong and violent, which do not suffer delay because it is feared of those who come with malice, that is greater than a small harm entering through the time.
And thus it is not considered in your souls, or, sons, that this is not esteemed by anyone but the common people and foolish doctors, so that to that disease which is cured by cautery, there is no reduction at any time, and they pause at the consequences.
And the cause is not thus as they say for that reason, because cautery is nothing but in a place of medicine which alters the condition and dries up the humors which are the cause why pains come.
But in any case, cautery is excessive over medicine because of the desire for its virtue and worthiness of its operation and greatness of its lord.
And it is possible that his disease will return at some hour of time, according to the condition of the patient and the location of his disease, and the virtue of it, and what is prepared in the body of him from the aggregation of superfluities in him, and what is obtained by him in his acquisition through foods and similar causes; except that the disease which is administered with cautery is a subtle disease in a few superfluities and humors, just like the cautery of the tooth for pain and similar to that, it is possible that in him the pain will not return, but rather it will be reduced in smallness.
And besides, the common saying is that cautery is the last resort of medicine, and it's a dreadful remedy, not to what they understand in it, because I believe that there is no cure that benefits by medicine or any other cause, approaching to cautery.
And the cause is contrary to that; and I understand that cautery is the last resort of medicine not at all when we administer the methods of healing in some diseases, and those medicines do not concur, and it approaches the end of the cause, then one administers cautery, and profits from it. And hours ago I said that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the understanding which I understand, and which the common people and foolish doctors also understand.
And they said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this except by the equality of gold and the subtlety of its substance.
And they said that the place of cautery does not make a difference, just as it is not absolutely true, for I have already proven and demonstrated that it does not do this except in some bodies or others, and cautery with gold is good and better than with iron just as they say; but however, when you do cautery with fire on gold, it is not declared to you, because it depends on the quantity that you want by the hardness of the gold, and because it prepares to receive heat; and if you adjust it above it, ignition occurs, and case some layers form so that the craftsman can see through the occupation of that.
And therefore, it is made to do cautery with iron in a way that is lighter and more proper for the rectitude of operation.
And I have arranged this chapter on cautery according to chapters, and I have arranged those from head to foot, so that the one seeking it may easily find what they want.
The First Chapter.
This cauterization brings relief to the humidity and coldness on the service of the accident of which there are two causes: one cause is soda and multiplicity of fluxes, called corissa, from the head to the partitions of the eyes and ears that flow, and multiplicity of sleepiness, and toothache and gout, and universally all disease that comes through coldness, just as paralysis, stroke, and apoplexy, and similar diseases in those illnesses.
The form of this cauterization is as follows: first, I command the patient to be purged with laxative medicine in the head, for three or four nights, according to what the virtue of the patient and their age and habit requires.
And then I command him to shave his head with a razor, and then make that section sit between his own hands on a covered bench, and have him rest his hands on the stones.
And then pause the razor's stroke at the tip of your thumb, right above the nostrils between his own eyes. But when the above said location is reached, mark that location with a tent, and then light the cautery olive of which this is the form:
And then pause that [cautery] on the marked location with the tent, in such a way that it descends gradually, as your hand is constrained little by little, and you turn it.
And then lift your hand slightly and look at the location, and if you see that some part of the skull has been uncovered, just like the amount of grain of errors, then lift your hand, and if it does not return to that iron [cautery], use another one, if it is chilled, until what I have told you is seen by the bone.
And then take a small amount of salt and dissolve it on the location and let it stay for three days.
And then pause over it, covered with a cloth in the border and let it stay until the scar of the fire is destroyed. And then cure the location with four-part medicine until it is healed.
And they said that when the wound remains open, so much the better, it gets the balm, because it is more suitable and beneficial.
And some of them said that the tongue should be cauterized inside the bone, and kept there until some part of the specificity of the bone is absorbed.
And then it should be removed from that which has been absorbed by the bone, and then it should be cured.
And others said that with the cautery, it should be brought to the end, until it presses strongly on the bone, until the bone cracks, and this is the form of little alfalfa: and they think that from that location, the vapors of the head will be released.
And the open wound should be kept for a long time, and then it should be cured until it is consolidated.
But to me, it is not seen in these two species of cautery from all, except in some men according to the way of fear; and leaving that, I must say that it is better for health when it is so, because the head is revealed by the solution of continuity like we have testified in other members, and especially when the patient's head is of fierce nature.
And the first species of cautery is more saved and better, it seems to me; and with that house and that work, there is health.
Second Chapter.
On Caustics for the Head.
When chronic and long-lasting pain occurs throughout the head in a patient who is prolonged in his malady, and uses of wars, warts, capillaries, poultices, emplasters, goutzes, cadels, and gualinas, and especially if it has already been cauterized with one cautery which relents and does not benefit the patient at all, then consider whether the head of the patient is of strong creation in his nature; and if it is not fierce and does not find great cold, then that other cauterizes another cauter, leaving a little bit. And then cauterize it on the crown of the patient's head with another cautery until the tongue is divided. Cut the tongue and uncover the quantity of bone which we have recounted, and cauterize it with one cautery in the back part of the head at the location called "vas", -- and that is the location where a ventose is placed. And lift your hand away from there, and do not uncover the bone, because the patient by this will feel a great pain different from the pain of all other head cauterizations.
And I say that this cautery is in its place, because it needs the cautery with which you cauterize the crown of the head and the occiput is more subtle than that with which the middle part of the head is cauterized; and this is its form.
Third Chapter.
On Caustics for Migraine Not of Ancient Origin.
When the patient has a headache in the back of the head, or it spreads to the eye, first purify the head with laxative medicines, and then administer the other cure which I have said in the divisions of diseases; and if none of these helps, then cauterization is done in two ways: either cauterization with acute medicine combined, or with iron.
But the cauterization with combined medicine is when you take a small amount of aloes, and extract it and cut off the extremities of both ends. And then cut the location of the pain in the temple with a well-sharpened knife until a small opening is made, leaving the tongue to be hidden.
And then strengthen it with a stopper pressed down by gradual constriction, and leave it for the space of three hours; and then remove the bandage and treat the aloes, and let the wound stay for two or three days, and then pause over it covered with a cloth until the location makes an opening.
And then cure that with four-part medicine until it is healed.
And if you wish, do this with some combined medicines which I have written in the two treatises on combined medicines.
But the cauterization with iron, according to this method: ignite for the purpose of which this is the form:
and is called "claw of nails", because the head of it is like a form of claw in which there is some curvature, and in the middle part of it is a small prominence.
And then pause on the location of the pain, and hold your hand - so that the iron is not absorbed into the bone which remains - and slowly turn the small iron with velocity.
And if the quantity of bone that is absorbed by the specificity of the tongue is like the majority of bone, and raise your hand for this reason, so that the artery which remains is not absorbed, so that there may not be a flow of blood.
And then soak the cloth in saltwater and pause it on the location, and leave it for three days; and then remove the cloth with a border, and cure with four-part medicine until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize at the tip of the knife according to the caustic, and be careful not to cut into the artery in this non-ancient migrainous pain.
Fourth Chapter.
On Caustics for Ancient Migraine.

However, it is necessary for you to be careful about the continuity of the jawbone, which is damaged by mastication, and that the ligament not be absorbed and the nerves that are affected by it, so that there is no spasming.
And if it is on the custody and caution of the flow of blood from the artery that is cut, because in the cutting of it there is fear, and especially to him who ignores what he does and is not studious and experienced; and leave the operation to begin.
And you will find in the remembrance of the regimen of blood flow accidental to the artery according to your method, in this book.

Fifth Chapter.
On Caustics for Earaches.
When in the ear there is pain due to cold and it is cured with laxative causes and with the other cure which I have said in the division, and if the pain is not relieved, then ignite the cauterizer, and this is called "punctum", the form of which is:
And then make the punctum and approach the ignition, and be carried around the entire ear like a wheel is rolled, or in the circuit of each example if the pain is in one. Hold the cauterizer at the root of the ear, little by little, until you have marked the location with intent.
And if the cauterizer touches all the points in the entire ear, and those ones, and then cure the locations until they are healed.
Sixth Chapter.
On Caustics for Itching.
Itching which is cured and with cauterization is only of the species that comes from flux, according to what we have said in the divisions of diseases.
Avoid cauterization of the species which occurs due to dryness or spasm of the nerve.
When you cure that species of itching with ointments and poultices and gualguaries, and your cure does not relieve the patient, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauterizers: one at the root of the ear, and the second a little below the temple, and the third at the conjunction of two lips.
And pause your cauterizer on the contrary side of the affected part, because softening only appears on the part that seems to be healing.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize it with the cauterizer on the right side of the extremity of the ear, slightly above the crown of the head, and on the temple another, the length of which is according to the length of the thumb's joint, and pause your hand with the cauterizer until the quantity of the majority of the bone's specificity is consumed.
And this is the form of the cauterizer, and it is a species of the knife cauter, the form of which is before us. But meanwhile, it is more subtle that you see only a little of what I have said; and it is necessary to cut away the excessive roughness in it a little.
And then cure the location with water as is before the process, until it is healed.
Seventh Chapter.
On Caustics for Ancient Apoplexy.
When apoplexy is ancient and you cure it with the water which we have said and your medicine does not relieve the patient and the patient has no fever, then cauterize that with four cauterizers: on all the horns of his head; and with a cauterizer in the middle part of the head, just as we have said; and with a cauterizer in the occiput. And the method of cauterization is done according to what was said above.
And already it has been cauterized on the mouth of the stomach; and it is more posterior; and then be cured with water as proceeds.
Eighth Chapter.
On Caustics for Oblivion caused by Flux.
Make sure that the patient is given in the beginning large quantities of ointments and pills serving as purgatives.
And then shave the head of the patient and pause on the occiput of it an emplaster described in the treatise on emplasters.
And pause that for several days, because that is the manner of cauterization. And do this according to the order which I have said before.
And therefore if it is good for those who are healed by this; and otherwise, then make three cauterizers on the posterior part of his head, which are descending from the uppermost part of the head to the lower part of the neck. And pause between each cauterizer the thickness of the finger, and then cure the cauterizer with water as has been done.
But if you add more and the patient is so tolerant, then make a cauterizer in the middle part; and if you wish to add even more, then immediately cauterize that on both horns.
And then cure that until it is healed; and be the cauterizer olive-shaped according to the form given before.
Ninth Chapter.
On Caustics for Paralysis and Softening of the entire Body.
Make sure that you process in softening the head with ointments and water as we have said; and then shave the head of the patient, and immediately cauterize it with a cauterizer in the middle part of the head, and with a cauterizer on all the horns of the head, and with a cauterizer on the posterior part of it, and with three cauterizers on the vertebrae of the neck.
And if it is necessary in the disease of softening of the body of many and the patients are tolerant and the disease is strong, then immediately cauterize that with four cauterizers on the vertebrae of the back, and afterwards with a cauterizer until it is burned through to the bone marrow, and lift up your hand. And then cure that until it is healed, and this be an olive-shaped cauterizer.
Tenth Chapter.
On Caustics for Epilepsy.
It is not cauterized the epileptic, but that epilepsy is caused by flux.
And therefore, make sure to soften the brain of the patient at the beginning with ointments and other cure which we have said in the division when the disease is great and the patient is tolerant except for medicines.
And if the child cannot tolerate medicines, then administer gualguaries and mastigatories which serve to soften, for several days, with good nourishment of food.

But if the patient is a child, then pause with a subtle cauterizer according to this method.

And then put that in the middle part of the head of him in the circle, and leave it until it is warmed through.

Twelfth Chapter.

Sixteenth Chapter.
On Caustics for the Eyelid of the Eye when the hairs are converted to the inner parts and punch the eye.
When the hairs of the eye are converted to the inner parts in such a way that they pierce the eye, cauterize them according to two methods: either by burning or by medicinal concoction.
If with a cauterizer of fire, command the patient before this that he shall look at his hairs in such a way as those which are softening, until they are prolonged and equalized; and if you punch that, let him have their natural growth, then you strengthen the eyes of him with a bandage so that it may not be harmed until the hairs are born.
Then when they are born and equalized, pause the patient's head in your seat, and then signal on the eyelid of his eyes with a tent, with a sign which is according to the figure of a leaf of mirta, and be the beginning of the sign close to the hairs.
And then wrap it in a cloth soaked with human urine or in mucus of papyrus on the eye.
And then ignite the cauterizer of which this is the form:
And then cauterize on the figure which is signaled, little by little, in many times, until the surface of the bone which is like a leaf of mirta, is completely burned through, appearing properly.
And the sign of health for this work is that you see the eyelid of the eye already contracted and the hairs of it being lifted above the point of puncture of the eye.
And then raise your hand and leave that for three days, and then pause on it with a cloth until the scar is raised. And then care for that with an ointment until it is healed.
But if some cause returns to the hairs for their natural growth and the eyelid is softened, then immediately do another time the cauterization on that just as you did previously.
But if the hairs are in the eyelid left behind, then immediately cauterize that until it is elevated to its natural place and equalized, so that the hairs do not pierce the eye.
But the cauterizer with medicinal concoction is this: you command the patient to look at his hairs until they are prolonged and equalized, and then make a cloth of fabric in the shape of a leaf of myrtle.
And then take one ounce of known sulfur and one ounce of living vinegar. The end! And then take one ounce of known sulfur and one ounce of living vinegar. Mix those causes well, and make that with fasting so that it is not warmed; and then spread that water over the cloth which is made in the shape of a leaf of myrtle, and pause that on one eye or both eyes; and pause afterwards the eye cloth wrapped in human urine, and the patient's head be in your seat.
And then pause the said thing on the medicine and press it a little and do not harm it until the patient feels the stinging of the medicine, for stinging is in it as if from fire.
And then when the patient perceives that he is feeling stinging, then immediately stop the medicine and wash it with your said water; therefore, when the stinging ceases, then again wash the eye with water; and then consider if the eyelid has been lifted as much as it was washed away by fire or incision, for then you are well; and if not, return to that same spot with the medicine where you did not apply the medicine before, and do not neglect until your operation is equalized and the eye is contracted.
And then pause on it with a cloth wrapped in a border until the bone of adjustment is eradicated; and then care for that with an ointment or another until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you to be diligent in your operation, watching carefully that the medicine does not fall into the eye; and if the eyelid becomes softened after some days and some cause of the hairs pokes into the eye, then immediately repeat your medicine on that spot where the eyelid is softened, and do exactly as you did at the beginning, and approach it until it is healed.
And this is the form of leaf of myrtle.
And know that the eyes of men are diversified according to their greatness and smallness, and therefore according to that is made your contraction.
And let not the way of righteousness be hidden from him to whom this art is studied in this book.
Seventeenth Chapter.
On Caustics for Fistulas that are in the Lachrymal of the Eye.
When you cure a fistula with water as we have said in the divisions of diseases and it does not correspond to your treatment, then consider that you must cauterize it according to this method: command the patient to pause his head in your seat, and hold the head of him some minister between your thighs in such a way that he is not harmed nor agitated with his own head.
And then wrap it in a cloth soaked in human urine or in mucus of papyrus on the eye of him.
And then ignite the cauterizer of which this is the form:
which is curved, like a shape of cane or of a vulture's beak, from one end where the cauterizer is made.
And if you wish, it should penetrate to the other end. And if you wish, it should be taken out like a tent.
But in any case, the one that is curved is better for your work.
And then press the fistula if it is open, and take out from it pus and dry up that one. And if it is not open, then immediately work on that and extract the discharge from it.
And then pause on it the cauterizer which is well ignited, and take with your hand a little of the cauterizer from the eye to the nose, so that you do not err or the patient becomes troubled, and then pause the cauterizer in the gray of the eye and corrupt that one.
And then if at the beginning of your cauterizer it enters into the bone, good is; and otherwise, immediately repeat the cauterizer one or two times, as needed; and leave that alone for three days, and then pause on that cloth wrapped in a border and surround it with an ointment to dry out until it is healed.
But if it is passed 11 days and it is not healed, then immediately pause on the sharp corrosive medicine until the bone is uncovered and shaved according to what is written in your own chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula which some earlier doctors also said: take the location of the fistula and fill it with it; and then pause in that fissure, subtle like this form: And pour into that the quantity of one ounce of melted lead; and hold your hand with a camal with good retention, and let not the patient be harmed because the melted lead does not reach the eye of that one; and it is necessary to pause on the patient's eye wrapped in human urine or water, for the lead adheres to the location of the fistula and heals it through marvelous healing.
And if the fistula is healed with what we have said about cauterization and treatment, good is; and otherwise, it is necessary to administer a blow through the nose and reduce the fistula to the body of the nose according to where it will come into its proper place.

Many times accidentally split fissures occur in the lips, and most commonly in the lips of children.

Nineteenth Chapter.
On Caustics for Fistulas in the Mouth.
When in the root of the uvula or on the palate or on the roots of the teeth there is an apostema and it grows, and breaks forth, and becomes antiquated, and a fistula forms, and you cure that one and it does not take effect, then consider that you must ignite the cauterizer according to the quantity received in the fistula; and then put that ignited instrument into the track of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches the bottom of it, and at the end of it make it thus one or two times; and then care for that with the water that we have said about treatment until it is healed.
And then if the pus is discharged and it is healed, good is; and otherwise, it is necessary to discover the location and uncover the corrupted bone according to what is written in its chapter.
Twentieth Chapter.
On Caustics for the Teeth and Softening of the Gums.
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth are harmed, and you cure those with medicines and they do not take effect, then pause the patient's head in your seat, and immediately ignite the cauterizer of which this form comes close to, so that you pause the quill on the tooth and introduce into it the ignited cauterizer quickly, and hold your hand a little until the patient feels the heat of the fire reach the root of the tooth.
And then lift up your hand, and immediately repeat the cauterizer several times according to what you wish.
And then the patient will rinse his mouth with saltwater and hold it for an hour, and afterwards stop, because the harmed tooth is closed, and the softened gum is strengthened, and the corrupted moisture is dried out.
Twenty-first Chapter.
On Caustics for Toothache.
When toothache is due to coldness, or there is frost or vermin in it, or the treatment with medicine does not take effect, then consider that cauterization in that case is according to two methods: either cauterization with a border of cow's milk, or cauterization with fire.
Cauteri am boder is that you take the border of cow's milk and boil it in a metal pot, then take a cloth and wrap it around the edge of the tent, and then immerse that boiled border in the cloth, and pause that on the painful tooth quickly until it is cooled.
And then immediately repeat that several times until the virtue of fire reaches the root of the teeth.
And if you wish, submerge a cloth or cloth in the border mentioned above, and pause that on the painful tooth, and then pause over that iron heated until the iron reaches the bottom of the cavity of the tooth.
But in any case, the cauterization with fire is that you wait for the quill of iron or metal to be heated red-hot and in its heart there is some grooves, and the sharpness of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient.
And then ignite the cauterizer in the shape that will come, and pause it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cauterizer is cooled; and do this several times until the pain is relieved or the next day.
And it is necessary that through the impression of that cauterizer, the patient will fill his mouth with good border and hold it for an hour and then spit it out; and this is the form of the cauterizer.
And cauterize as you wish, to the extent that it is possible for you.
And this is the form of the quill:

And if the apostema is small, then pause the cauterizer according to the quantity of the apostema; and then let it be for three days and pause over it a cloth wrapped in border until what the fire has burned out is relived.
And then care for that with an ointment, tents, and cloths until it is healed.

Twenty-seventh Chapter.
On Caustics for the Foot Fret.
When the foot is affected by pain due to coldness or humidity or excessive sweating, and it has departed from its normal state through excessive evacuation, and the patient has not been cured with water as we have said, then consider that the patient should be placed on his back over his navel, and sense with tendons three cauterizers according to this form and this quantity pressed onto the foot below the hip bones, in which lies the seat of man.
And be the space between each cauterizer according to the thickness of the finger, and let the cauterizers be according to the length of the straight arm.
And do not compress the flesh with the cauterizer.

Twenty-eighth Chapter.
On Perforation of Apostema of the Foot with a Cauterizer.
When you need to excise or perforate an apostema on the foot and you want to know if that apostema is in the flesh of the foot or in its skin, then if it is in the flesh of the foot, the patient will be troubled by gravity and pain without sharpness.
And if it is in the skin of the foot, with great pain and many times that you have exhausted the doctors' cure.
Therefore, consider that the patient should be placed on his back over his navel; and immediately sense the location of the apostema with tendons; and immediately ignite the cauterizer which is assembled like a rag, its form having been described in another page. And then cauterize with that and the cauterizer until all the vertebra is burned, until it reaches the navel, until it becomes a healthy wound.
And immediately care for that one with treatment of other apostemas until it is healed.
And do not consider that this form of cauterization should be used except by one who has prolonged his study in the art of medicine and has known many diseases; but as for this one, it is bold at times on this operation, but yet leave that to us, and may it be so.
Twenty-ninth Chapter.
On Caustics for Pleurisy.
They said the ancient ones that the cauterizers of the roots of aristology should be made for pleurisy from cold and dry roots according to this manner; and it is this: take a root of aristology long and dry that is found, and it is as thick as a finger.
And immediately submerge it in oil and ignite it at the fire, and then cauterize with a cauterizer on that location which is between the continuation of the furcula and the neck; and with two small cauterizers left guiding, one slightly declining towards the side below the beard, and with two cauterizers in the area that is declining between the fifth rib and the navel, declining slightly behind; and with another cauterizer in the middle location of the foot; and with one on the stomach, and with three cauterizers behind; and with one cauterizer on that location which is between the two shoulders, and with two cauterizers on both sides of the foot, left guiding the cauterizer which is between the two shoulders.
And do not compress your hand with the cauterizer, but rather in the manifestation of the vertebra in work.
And already some ancient ones have said that among certain men who use a cauterizer of iron similar to a ray and ignite it, and put it in the location which is between the ribs, until it reaches that apostema and purulent matter is discharged, just as we have said in the apostema of the foot.
But in this perforation with a cauterizer there is no fear, for he who does so will soon afterwards find himself in the location of fistula which is not susceptible to healing.
Thirtieth Chapter.
On Caustics for Malaria.
When you cure the disease of malaria with water as we have said in the division and do not confirm your cure, then consider that the cauterization is done in three ways, all of which are drying, one of which is that you make three or four lines according to the length of the malarial fever, following the figure of the cauterizers of the foot, whose figure has preceded.
And between each cauterizer be the thickness of a finger or slightly more, and the manner of the cauterization be the same manner which we have said in the cauterizers of the foot, alike.
And do not compress your hand with the cauterizer; and the patient should be lying on his back.
And there is another way of cauterizing, so that you ignite the cauterizer having two vertimentz, which cause we have said in the chapter on dislocation of the muscle, and lift up the vertebra which is in the endright of the malaria, where the patient's left side is seized.
And be your elevation by which you elevate the vertebra according to the length of the body, so that the cauterizers may be made according to the latitude of the body.
And immediately insert the two vertimentz, ignite the middle one, so that with those you penetrate the vertebra from the other side.
And immediately extract the cauterizer; and therefore four cauterizers are made.
And if you wish, cauterize with a cauterizer having three vertimentz.
And immediately take care of the cauterizer so that it does not lay waste for too many days, because it is more certain than the other previous causes in healing.
Thirty-first Chapter.

Cauterizers are not applied in hydrocephalus, but rather in acute cases proper.

And the quantity of the depth of the cauterizer should be proportioned to the subtlety of the vertebra.
And immediately leave the cauterizer unburied, so that it may remain for a long time.
And do not evacuate the patient's cure by cauterization with water as is necessary, so that two intentions are added to it, and it is hastened with the help of healing.
The form of the cauterizer with which the belly is cauterized is cleft-like, according to the form that has preceded it, and it is this one with which the back is cauterized is olive-shaped, according to its previous form.

Thirty-sixth Chapter.

Dry out all the blood with a sponge or cloth, and immediately fill between the two lips of the incision with old cuttlebone or cloths dipped in vinegar. And immediately press down upon those pulpits filled with vinegar and oil, so that there may not be an outflow of cauterized aposteme.
And when you have removed this and see that the aposteme is diminished, then it is good to press upon the bone until it begins to appear as flesh, and immediately cure it with an emplastrum exsiccatiu which makes the flesh appear, just as if you took two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony and mixed them together, and from this make a poultice and administer it in these wounds at the time of the natural birth of flesh.
Sixth Chapter.
On the Cure of that which Catarrhs in the Ears.
The total cause that catarrhs in the ears is one of four species, for either it is mineral pyrrhea or a similar cause like iron and verdigris, or it is from plant material like cypress or fava, or it is a fluxible cause like water and vinegar mixed together with their likenesses, or some beast.
And therefore, when pyrrhea or another similar cause that does not agree with the ear catarrhs in the ear, and pause the ear at the sun, and if sometimes the pyrrhea appears, then immediately distill some oil of violet or samama into it, and administer the extraction from there, and make the stornutation according to condition, and block the nostrils beforehand by the event of stornutation. And immediately pause in the cavity of the ear some cloths or wool, and stretch the ear to the parts above, because many times it is forgotten with these causes.
And if not, then immediately administer the extraction from there with the instrument called gestae epicicarios, of which this is the form:
And if forgotten with gestae, be it so; and otherwise, immediately administer the extraction from there with a subtle onyx of few duplications.
And therefore, if not forgotten by this, then immediately make a needle of iron and insert the extremity of the needle into the hole of the ear and close around the needle with wax and softened oil so that only the needle is left. And immediately extract the instrument with strong attraction, for too many times as we have recounted.
But if not forgotten in this manner, then immediately take a halved light or a prepared vessel with which the hawks grasp a small quantity, and pause that in the extremity of the ray, and immediately envelop it with a decently placed cut. And immediately insert that into the hole of the ear with ease, and immediately dry out the ear from its humidity.
And therefore, if not forgotten with all the causes which we have recounted, then you should cut it down before it becomes cauterized or spasmed.
And the manner of cutting it down is that you first bleed the patient from the saphena vein and extract the blood according to the virtue of the matter, and immediately make it cease between your hands and convert the ear to the parts above, and then make a small incision in the root of the ear at the location where the grey matter is previously prepared. And the incision should be of lunar shape until it reaches the pyrrhea, and when the pyrrhea is blackened, stop that if you can with suitable instruments; and immediately close the incision at that hour with speed, and cure that so that it may be healed.
And if the cause that afflicts the ear is one of the fat things that increase and are inflated, then immediately administer the cure and extraction from there; but if it does not obey your command to come out, then you take a spatula of fine tin according to this form: and administer with that the cutting away of that fat thing which is fallen into the ear.
And do not make it when you think that it has already been moistened by the vapor of the ear, and pause it in many places, and then immediately extract it from there with onyxes or subtle gestures, or with incision as we have said, for it is alleviated the extraction from there.
But in the water that has entered the ear, it is good for the patient to use stornutation according to condition at first, and fill their own ear with a little old cuttlebone, and then place a stone above that ear where the water is, and if forgotten, be it so; otherwise, take many sharp iron points and lemons of the same length as the finger, heat them in the fire for a while, and then have the patient insert one of those into the hole of their own ear and strike another point on the stone that is opposite the ear where the water has entered. Therefore, do not cease until all the water has been forgotten.
Therefore, do not cease until all the water has been forgotten. And already the water will be forgotten in this way that you take a piece of paper or parchment. and place one end of it in the ear and stretch the other end over the fire until the middle of it is burned.
and immediately place another piece of parchment and make it so many times until all the water is forgotten, and extract that with a needle as we have said above regarding the extracting pyrrhea.
But if in the extraction of beastiness that enters into that ear, it is a small thing, like this and similar, cure that as we have said in the division; but if it is from great body which appears on the sense of the vessel, then immediately administer the extraction from there with gestures and onyxes, and the cause of it is more gentle than all the other causes that afflict the ear.
But if in the extraction of vermin generated in the ear, when you cure that with what we have said in the division and in the treatise on distillations, and your cure does not take hold, then it is good for you to gaze at the ear towards the sun.
And therefore, if any cause of the worms appears here, then immediately extract that with gestures or subtle onyxes; but if no cause appears, then take a needle made of straw and broad at the top of which this is the form: And insert the subtle end into the ear according to the quantity that the patient can tolerate; and immediately suck out with it a strong sucking motion, and do this many times, until all the worms are forgotten.
But if it does not obey your command to come out, then you should block and close the circuit of the needle with wax as we have said; then immediately administer distillations which have already been tried by the ancients in the cure of worms, and you will find this in the treatise on distillations.
And be your effusion with which you pour the medicinal oils into the ear with this instrument of which this is the form: And make that of silver or iron, made from straw, with a small hole in it and a flat top.
And thus be as they pour into the cavity of the needle's container, here where it is necessary. And if you wish, take the ray and wrap it around the end of the needle decently cut, and immediately drop oil into the cavity of the ear, or juice from some herb, or what you want from these medicines in the needle  and that is in the ear , and immediately insert the ray with a cut above and press it gently with your hand on the compression of the matter so that the oil is expelled into the cavity of the ear and the patient feels the oil flowing out.
And what is inserted in the ear has already been heated by fire for a little while. And be careful that the cause which you distill into the ear is not too hot, for the medicines of the ear cannot endure this.
Seventh Chapter.
On the Cure of Obstruction of Ears.
Sometimes certain children are born with the vents of their mothers not perforated, and this already happens in some men, obstruction in the meat of the ear due to a wound or flesh not having been there; and this obstruction sometimes is made in the forepart of the trunk of the ear which does not consent to the vessel, and sometimes it is in the outer parts.
And that which happens in the forepart of it, which does not comprehend the vessel, is in the most difficult dispositions for cure.
And when you succeed in comprehending the vessel, it is good that you pause the ear of the patient to the sun and gaze at it. And therefore, if there is an evident obstruction, open that with a subtle spatula of which this is the form:
If the end of it is in which there is a small latitude, where one part is acute and the other not; and the spatula is two-edged like a lion's tooth, for so that it does not cause harm to the ear.
And therefore, if the obstruction is due to flesh born in the ear or in the meat of it, then you should extract that with subtle onyxes and cut through that with a vehement ease until all the flesh is removed.
And if the obstruction is in the forepart of the ear, then you should take a subtle iron ray and heat it slightly with fire, and immediately place that into the meat of the ear.
And therefore, if you have detected obstruction by that which the patient finds with ease, due to gravity of hearing, force the oppression of it with ease; and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear.
And immediately pause in the ear with cloth of linen according to the quantity of the width of the hole which you have wrapped around it with Egyptian ointment; and do this for some days until you are sure of the consolidation of the wound; or take some white lead and soak it in water and powder over it, followed by use; and if the ear has already become apostemated, then it is good that you remove the lead and replace it with another lead which you wrapped around it with rose oil, until the aposteme becomes calm; and immediately cure that until it is healed.
But if bleeding occurs, then immediately immerse a sponge or cloth in hot water and pause it over the ear, and use the other cure which restricts the flow of blood, which is said in the treatise on distillation.
Eighth Chapter.
On the Cure of Athelis which affect the Eyelids.
Athelis which afflict the eyelids of men sometimes are humid, and at other times dry.
Therefore, it is good that you take those with ten-handles or onyxes, and incise them with an spatula of the roots, and immediately pause over the places as said.
But if pain accompanied by bleeding comes, then you should cauterize those with a lunar cauterizer of subtle onyx.
And the best cauterization is to do it immediately after the incisions and many times return when there remains some cause of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
Ninth Chapter.
On the Cure of Grandessia which comes to the Eyelids of Men.
Many times it happens that in the eyelids of men some cause arises which is akin to Grandessia in its strength and hardness, and because of this Grandessia is called.
And it is an accumulation of thick moisture on the eyelid below and above.
Therefore, the operation in them is that you should consider whether Grandessia is proceeding from there on the eyelid and is manifesting on all sides; and the cause of it is light.
Therefore, make an incision on that with a fissure by the latitude, and immediately cut it off from all sides with ease; and immediately suspend it with an onyx and cut off the excess.
And if the figure is large, then you should adjust it with a suture; and cure that until it is healed.
And if it is small, then you will not suffer harm from it because the ointment of it restores that and enfleshes.
And if Grandessia is declining towards the outer parts of the eyelid, then you should remove the surface outside, and immediately ease the eyelid and suspend Grandessia with an onyx, unless you are forced to make an incision; and press that from all sides, and if the eyelid through incision is lengthened, this will not help in any cause.
And immediately after the incision, wash the eyes with salty water; and cure the place with that which enfleshes until it is healed.
Tenth Chapter.
On the Cure of Axcirnach in the Eyelid above the Eye.
Axcirnach is a grayish substance which is generated in the tunic of the eyelid above, and more often affects children, aggravating their eyes and causing them to weep; and they cannot look at the brightness of the sun because tears are shed upon them.
And for this reason you must always wet their faces and sleep on their faces, so that the eyelids of theirs below are covered with humidified skin, which has already been inflamed, and there is imminent danger of apparent inflammation in the eye; and when you press the place with those words, you will cause inflammation within them.
And some manner of operation is in that which the patient places their head on the tie and you immediately place a cloth of linen and oil there, making a calque, and make from it a circle according to the quantity which contains Axcirnach from all sides, and immediately place that upon that and press with those words so that inflammation may be aggregated in the middle of the circle, and immediately end in the middle of that humidity with a spatula incised with a fissure by latitude, and the fissure not be greater than the one made in flautobotomy.
But in the forepart it is good that you make a cut all around until you reach the inflammation, because in the most desperate cases, inflammation proceeds by fissure according to the form of white grayseness.
Therefore, extract that with cloths which you have wrapped between the said ties to the outer parts and revolve it between your right and left hand until it is scattered.
And be careful not to insert into the fissure, lest with the spatula you do not reach the eye and disturb it.
But if there is no appearance of Axcirnach at the beginning of the fissure, but rather you adjust into the fissure a little with ease, so that Axcirnach may proceed; and immediately extract that as we have said; and immediately submerge cloths in water, vinegar and powder, and pause those over the place and strengthen them with polvils.
And thus some will trickle salt and pause it in the cavity of the fissure, so that what remains of that humidity may be dissolved.
And immediately cure that until it is healed.
But if there is an apostemate in the place which becomes calm, then you should cure that with soft plasters until it is healed.
Eleventh Chapter.
On Methods of Touching the Eye.
When in the eyelids of men there are born natural folds, and so becoming antiquated, then they no longer touch the eye and cause methods of illnesses such as constant tears and softening of the eyelids and skin, until this becomes a cause of destruction of the eye which is called touching the eye, and it is cured in four ways: or by cauterization with fire; or by acute medicine according to what has been said before in the chapter on cauterization; or by atactini made through incision and suture; or by canna according to what I will say.
And therefore it is good that you pause the head of the patient in the tie; immediately convert the eyelid of the eye with your left hand, and if it is converted, then it is well; and if not, insert a needle into that part which is nearest to the edge of the eyelid on the side where there are no hairs - namely, among the hairs themselves - and make the needle penetrate above, and thus - near the margin of the eyelid - pull out the thread to the upper parts with the eyelid, and convert it with a ray.
And immediately end in the outer part of the eyelid below the hairs with a spatula incised with lacrimal major into the lacrimal minor; and immediately extract the thread and pause below the eyelid with small powder or cloth, and immediately shut over the eyelid with a tent, and it will be thus as the figure of myrtle leaves.
But nonetheless it is good that the figure be according to the quantity of elevation of the eyelid, because this has already been diversified in men, since some of them require that a great quantity of the eyelid be incised according to the quantity by which the eyelid is softened.
And immediately end with the spatula on both lines which you have drawn, and begin from the lacrimal major into the lacrimal minor. And if your incision is like the natural folds as they are in the king's beard.
And immediately place the onyx in one of the two angles of the wound, and immediately extract all that, and adjust with a suture the two lips with a gulf or fine woolen thread, and absorb the blood, and make adhere what is superfluous from the threads to two eyebrows with some perceiving causes; if you wish to do so, and otherwise, do not cure.
And immediately loosen the thread of the threads within three or four days, and immediately cure that.
And if you wish, leave the wound without suture, and cure that with what dries up and constricts, because the eyelid is elevated by the sealing of the wound and its aggregation; but suturing is better. And thus I say to those who came before me to taxine.
But nonetheless in him there is solicitude for the patient, and it is of good operation, and not in him fear.
And it is another manner in taxine, and it is that you mark on the eyelid a figure as of myrtle leaves, and immediately elevate the eyelid with three unctuous substances separated and congregate according to this form:
But if it is not possible to have the unctuous substances, and this is not equalized, then take a needle with thread and insert it into the middle of the figure, and enter the other thread alongside the lacrimal major, and the second thread alongside the lacrimal minor, and adjust between the said ties the threads with equality, and immediately elevate your hand with elevating motion, elevate all the wound over which is marked as we have recounted.
And immediately adjust the two lips of the wound with a suture, and cure that until it is healed.
But if there occurs an apostemate because of your incision or your fissure, then calm that apostemate with cerote and oil-like substances, and with gentle remedies.
And sometimes it happens that the eyelid is converted so that its hairs are turned, then it is good that you use in that what we have said about incision; but suture in each case is more artificial.
Atactining with canna is according to this form: and it is that you convert the eyelid and cut out the figure which is outside according to what I have recounted; and immediately make two cannae or two fine astals, the length of which is according to the length of the eyelid and the latitude of which is less than the latitude of the spatula. And you have already incised at the extremities of each part, where you have the threads.
And immediately add each one with subtlety on top of what superfluously protrudes from the eyelid of the eye, and constrict the cannae of each part with a very tight stricture, and leave it for some days, because the wound will die and become denuded and will fall inwards as it slowly descends.
But if it is delayed, then tear off the threads, and immediately cure the wound until it is healed.
Therefore, when it is solidified, the eyelid is elevated and the hairs do not prick.
And this is the form of two cannae which you will make according to this form: and have the quantity of length and latitude neither more nor less.
Twelfth Chapter.
On the Elevating of Pricking Hairs in the Eye with a Needle when the Hair is Hard.
When the hairs are unnatural, hard and rough, and prickly to the eyes, the operation in that is that you take a fine needle and pause it in that delicate thread of silk or wool, and immediately adjust the extremities of it so that they fit together in a manner most subtle. And be the length of the threads of the quantity of one palm.
And immediately compose another fine thread below it in brief, and tie the extremities of that if you wish.
And immediately place the patient's head in the tie and it be proper for the sun, so that your work may be declared, because it is a subtle and minute operation.
And immediately insert the needle into the root of the adjusted hair which has required engineering, and make it penetrate into the eyelid rapidly until you extract it above the natural hair.
And immediately pull out the hair upwards and insert it into the alloy, and be the hairs one, two, or three, but not more.
And immediately pull out your hand with that until the hair is extruded and alloyed in the eyelid along with the natural hair.
But if the alloy is attracted and not expelled the hair, you will attract the alloy to the parts below along with the thread which you have composed there, until it is expelled above the superfluous part.
And gaze at that with the vision of the eye, because then you will expel the alloy and the thread, and grate all and close the eye, and leave the closures for two or three days, until the hair adheres to its place and grows well on top of it.
And if the hair is too short, then you adjust one long hair from the natural hairs, and it is elevated with that, or let it be until it grows to a suitable space, and then you elevate that.
Thirteenth Chapter.
On the Cure of Echachration which appears on the Eyelid above.
When there appears in the eye Echachration, which is contraction of the eyelid when it is contracted on one side or the other, either above, below, to the right or left, due to bad consolidation of a wound or section or cauterization, and it is called Leporina, and this Echachration either occurs naturally or accidentally, and it is caused by consolidation of a wound or sections or cauterizations, or by resemblance to their maladies.
The manner of the operation in this is that you open up that consolidation and separate the lips of it, and pause within it a piece of linen cloth, and bind those together until they are healed.
And it is not good that you use a cure for this of the causes which dry up and constrict; because if you do so, it will return to echachration worse than never had any.
Use in that a cause which softens, such as fenugreek, and mix with the water in which it is cooked, or with a gentle poultice of aquilon, which is liquefied with some of the oils, and submerge the cloth in that, and cure with that.
And the treasure of your cure is that you perforate with all artifice that is not consolidated according to the form which it had at the beginning.
And this operation which we have said, is nothing but some correction of echachration that does not return to the form of the place as it was before.
Fourteenth Chapter.
On the Cure of Echachration which is made in the Eyelid below.
This echachration which is made in the eyelid below, which is truly called vertadierament echachration; and it is either of natural or accidental origin.
But accidental is made by wound or section or cauterization or other similar things.
And the way of the operation is that you take a needle with double thread, and put it into the flesh, and make it pass from the left lacrimal to the right lacrimal, until the thread reaches both extremities of the flesh.
And immediately extend the flesh to the upper parts with the needle and sew it with the needle, and incise with a spatula broad. And therefore if the figure of the eyelid returns as it should, it is good; and otherwise, take a ray and pause it in the cut figure, and with that convert the eyelid, and close the two incisions on the underside of the eyelid.
And be the extremities of the two incisions at two angles of the incision which you have made, where they converge, and be of their own making an angle, so that when they come together, a figure is formed by them.
And this figure is the Greek letter lambda ().
And immediately stop the flesh there by the quantity that is the thickness of the eyelid below, so that it may be cut.
And immediately adjust the separated parts and sew those with a thread of wool; and immediately cure those with what we have said about softening medicines and poultices, until it is healed.
And if echachration occurs due to fissure or suture or cauterization, then it is necessary that you open with a flat incision on the hairs of the eyelid according to what has been said before. And immediately separate with a poultice between two lips according to what we have said.
In the sum of the sermon on the cure of echachration when it is above or below, let the operation run its course according to what has been prepared in the form of echachration, and that is in the form of various modes.
And the skilled artisans prepare artfully in every manner possible for each case, so that they may return the figure to its natural form or almost, and that patient according to what is convenient for the operation and the instruments in the greatest dispositions.
Fifteenth Chapter.
On the Adherence of the Eyelid to the Conjunctiva or Cornea.
When this consolidation occurs in many men, it is necessary that the eyelid be solidly fixed above on the album of the eye, and prohibited from the ease of movement and its natural works, therefore it is necessary that you enter the extremity of the ray below the eyelid, and raise or extend it upwards with an unguent.
And immediately you incise the adherence with a spatula subtle, which is not sharp-edged, having a obtuse small part so that the patient may not be troubled by the operation, and leave the spatula so that it does not injure the eye in its subtlety.
And be your incision such that it excises that adherence with facility, so that the eyelid may return to its natural form and all the adherence may be healed.
And immediately you put in the eye salted water with which you wash, or distill into it zymic substances dissolved in water.
And immediately separate between the eyelid and the eye with a poultice of wool, and pause on the eye lanolin infused into the albumen of egg whites, and immediately use for three days causes that consolidate until it is healed.
Sixteenth Chapter.
On the Incision of the Ungue and Eminence of Flesh of the Lacrimals.
Know that the ungue is according to two manners, because it is either nervous, similar to a hard and subtle cipha, or non-nervous, similar to white congealed humidity, which when it touches iron, or is forced to take on oil, it is abscinded and the oil is not fixed in place.
And both species do not begin until the lacrimal major, which gradually covers the vision and prohibits light and movement of the eye.
But the manner of working in this incision is that the patient puts their head in the tie and you immediately open the eyes of them, and elevate the eyelid with your hand, and immediately collect the ungue with oil of little duplication and extend it to the upper parts. And immediately take a needle and enter it into that ungue with a horse or ox or cow hair, or similar thread, or a strong thread, doubling the extremity of the needle little by little and placing it in the middle of the ungue, and penetrate it with the needle, and tie it with thread to the ungue; and extend it to the upper parts, and excise on the side of the ungue which is before the pupil. And thus you follow that with the hair until the end of it.
And immediately you incise the remaining part at the root of the lacrimal with a subtle spatula or small forceps, and lift up the natural flesh of the lacrimal so that by this incision there may not be continuous flows of tears.
And sometimes the ungue with its extended oil or thread, as we have said, and immediately it is excised with a lion's spatula, the form of which is this:
And be careful that with the spatula you do not touch the corneal tunic and cause a rupture in it, and that the pupil is perforated.
And immediately the incision causes in the eye a little salt to be extracted or made from the juice of the sinic tree, and leave it until the next day; and immediately cure that with water as needed until it is healed.
And if the ungue is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle, nor is it fixed with oil in that place, then many times this species of ungue is cured by medicines, and is healed thus as I have said and recounted in the division.
And if you want to incise that, then you work on the eye of the patient and take a subtle lion spatula with keen edge according to this form: with subtlety. And if sometimes it is rarefied and is confused and enters into its root, then you distill from your own sight into the eye of sinic tree or with rose petal or with salted salt, and anoint the eye until the next day.
And immediately iterate over that the operation until all that is of it is remade, except that the contrary apostema may be in the eye, because then you leave it, and cure the apostema at the beginning until it is healed.
And immediately iterate your operation on that with reason until it is healed.
The Eminence of the lacrimal flesh, if noted in the eye for great harm, is suspended with oil; and you incise that from one part, and do not complete the incision so that you may not excise continuous flows of tears.
And immediately distill into the lacrimal rose petal and sinic tree until it is healed.
Seventeenth Chapter.
On the Incision of Algae and Water that is born from Adjusted Flesh in the Eye.
Sometimes in the eyes of some people there is born red flesh, and it is overgrown to cover the pupil, or approaches or strengthens above the eyelids and firmly compresses the eyelids against the parts outside and is assembled like a rose of balcony.
But the operation in this is that the patient puts their head in the tie; and immediately opens the eyes of that and collects all that flesh with suitable oils and water, and then anoints it with a forceps or with a basket; and immediately incises the flesh at the beginning until everything is finished with the encisor, and be careful not to injure the eye by your operation.
And be your incision with which you incise those or with spatula which we have recounted in the incision of the ungue, or with small forceps with which is collected according to the form that will come to this chapter.
And then when your incision is completed and all that flesh is remade, immediately fill the eye with salted salt, or distill into it red powder and resembling those of corrosive medicines, and pause on the outside of the eye covered with albumen of egg whites until it is ensured against apostema caution.
And if there remains some cause of algae and is sealed with caution, and you fear apostema caution, then immediately leave the eye alone and cure that apostema with water that will heal that apostema, and immediately iterate over it with operation until it is healed, and similarly do in the adjusted flesh which occurs in the eye of this species.
But however, you must ensure that the entire cure of the eye is through natural or accidental means, and not with iron, and do not put your hand in any of these operations until you see that member being sufficient for that operation.
Eighteenth Chapter.
On the Collection of Scales on the Eye.
Scales which come forth red and rough on the eye and prohibit its operation, and disclose the eye with the length of days.
Therefore it is necessary at the beginning that you consider whether the eye in which scales are present is strong and there is no other illness except scales, then you collect those scales.
And it is that you command the patient to put their head in the tie and immediately suspend those veins with one or two oils according to your prudence, and let that oil be of subtle duplication according to this form:
or two oils gradually mixed together in a vessel according to this form:
And immediately those veins are collected with subtle forces, with subtlety, and washed hour by hour, until you see those veins being remade from the eye and turned back.
And be careful that you do not injure the eye with the extremities of the spatula; and if your operation is in the middle of the day before the sun, and be firm in your operation that you only incise those veins.
And when you have completed, immediately you distill into the eye green or red powder so that with its keenness it may corrode the water that is remade from the scales.
But if this is not possible for you, collect everything in that hour, and immediately apply all the water that relieves the pain of it, and leave it for some days until the pain of it is calmed down and it is ensured against caution.
And immediately iterate over it in the same manner until it is healed.
And this is the form of the forceps:
Nineteenth Chapter.
On the Reduction of Nasal Discharge to the Nose.
When you cure nasal discharge with cauterization or acute medicine, as it is preceded by the narration of it and is not healed, then do not intervene in it except that you make an incision over the apostema until its maturity, and extract all the moisture which is in it and pour it into a container until the bone is revealed.
And then when the bone is revealed and corruption or blackness occurs in it, immediately you scrape it with an instrument of which this is the form:
And it is called the "Asper Cap", and is made of iron, and has a head rounded like an asher that is made pointed by lime or aliskalfati for subtle punctation (such as it is in this form).
And pause that over the corrupted part of the bone, and immediately rotate it between the said ties, and press your hand little by little until you know that corruption is scraped.
And then it is done several times, and immediately restore the place with causes of drying and purging.
Therefore if the place is consolidated and good flesh has grown in it, and the body of the pus has been removed and there are no more than 40 days, and it does not renew itself nor become apostematized, and no accident occurs in it, then you will know that it is healed.
And if not, then immediately do not intervene in it except to reduce the fissure to the form of the nose, and according to this manner: and is that you uncover the second bone with iron or acute medicine, and when it is uncovered, then you take a trip according to this form:
Be the extremity of the iron triangular, and the shaft of it be first exhausted up to the extremity thus as it is sometimes.
And immediately pause that over the bone, and be it close to the lacrimal; and lengthen your hand a little from the eye, and immediately turn your hand with the trip until it penetrates all the bone, and that feels the patient by sensing that something is going to come out through which they are going to feel pain.
Therefore immediately restore the place with purgative medicines that dry, just as if it were a poultice.
Therefore when the flesh and the place are hardened, immediately the material that was flowing to the parts outside returns to the nose, therefore it is easier on the patient.
Twentieth Chapter.
On the Reduction of the Eminence of the Eye.
When the eye eminences to its total height and there is no accident or diminution in it, then you must loosen the patient, and immediately follow, and pause for vaporous breathing in the cervix without scarification and suck well; and immediately pause over the eye with a liniment made from acacia, aloe, and sarcocolla, and strengthen the poultice on the eye with many powders.
And the manner of the powders is that you take cloths of lion's mane, and each cloth be duplicated into four folds; and make powder from those.
And immediately pause those one on top of the other according to the quantity which the eye needs. And immediately strengthen on those with a cloth of hard and strong texture; and iterate the bellows with suction without scarification; and immediately stop the bellows and leave the eye straight for the day and night.
But if in the meantime the ligament is softened, then you must immediately make it tight.
And immediately stop the ligament at the day and night as we have said.
And if the eye is already reduced, good it is; and otherwise, then immediately repeat the poultice with powders, tightening and bellows until it is healed.
Twenty-First Chapter.
On the Incision of the Eminence of the Uveal Tunic.
When there is a disruption in the uveal tunic and it is elevated and proceeds outside the palpebras like a grain of raisin, and its shape resembles that of a man due to this, and you want to incise it, then the operation in it is done as we have recounted, which is that you insert the needle into the root of the uvea from the part left and the part above, and immediately put the other needle into the double thread of the lacrimal part, and make that penetrate and leave the first needle according to its disposition; and immediately incise the location of the double thread and lift with it the part of the uvea in the circuit of the needle, and strengthen it firmly.
And immediately extract the needle and pause over the eye with lanolin infused in egg whites, and leave it until the thread dissolves into the uvea.
And immediately cure the eye with water that comforts it until the wound is healed.
And sometimes gather from all parts with a circle of cloth into the eye adjusted to great elevation, and immediately be perforated with a subtle spatula that comes to the prominence of the eye, and flow the humectant substance albuginea, and descend the eye and enter soon.
And immediately strengthen until it is healed.
Twenty-Second Chapter.
On the Cure of Alconati.
This illness, which is called Alconati, is nothing more than pus that is adjusted in the eye resembling water descending and it is not that.
But the manner of working on it is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, and immediately take their head in your hands from two parts, and make them look into the pus as if they were looking at something; and immediately make it dry and not descend, and be quiet the light, and the patient sees the causes just as they see.
And if it does not descend below, you will know that it is water.
But if it is not prepared for the descent of the pus with water as we have said, then immediately make the patient sit between your hands and take a subtle spatula and find it on the panniculus cerning a small piece, that is to say, the continuation of the conjunctiva with the tunic cornea in the crown (to the location you see), until the pus is forgotten.
Therefore when it is forgotten, then you distill into the eye water cooled in which you have mixed honey or water in which you have brewed fenugreek and honey.
And immediately cure with other causes until it is healed.
Twenty-Second Chapter (again).
On the Cure of the Water Descending from the Eye.
We have already said the species of water in the division and which is suitable for perforation as we are declaring, then use that according to its suitability.
Then you must make the patient sit between your hands on a cushion and tie their own eye tightly with a string.
