Therefore, when you see those signs, it is necessary that the belly of the child be compressed so that the fetus descends slightly, and when they come out on its head, they are delivered to it, and it is cleansed of those superfluities with good cleansing.
But that which is another part is non-natural and not to be trusted, for when the fetus is delivered with its feet first and the child's body is delivered in front of its head and its feet, one hand or at the foot... or is delivered with the head of the child and one hand or at the belly of the child, and very rarely it is turned on its back, and resembling the figures of non-natural childbirth.
Therefore it is necessary that the midwife be wise and subtle in all those causes, and that she guard against error and deception.
And I am showing you all the figures of those, and what power is in them, so that they may be significant by this and stand on that.
When the child is born on its head by natural extraction, and it is vehement over the woman and made to part with difficulty, and sometimes the virtue of the woman is already debilitated, then accordingly make that one cease, or what women have, and evaporate the menses with fenugreek and humectant oils.
And accordingly insert the midwife between her said small spatula and a slit in that one, or cut that one with its own nail until it flows forth what is in her of humidity. And press the woman's belly until the fetus descends.
But if it doesn't descend, then accordingly the woman should be anointed with mummy of papyrus and mummy of fenugreek mixed with camomile.
And accordingly command her to be anointed with it, and accordingly the anointing should be compressed and make that one sneeze with conditions; and take away her mouth and nose from her for an hour, because the fetus will soon forget about it.
And if two of the fetus's hands are forgotten at the beginning, then accordingly you should reduce those with small ease little by little. But if it does not obey the instrument, then accordingly pause the woman on a pillow and lift her feet up, and accordingly conceive the pillow on the earth; and the woman should be held so that she does not fall from the concussion.
And if the hands are not returned and the fetus dies, then accordingly insert those and extract the remnant of the fetus or tie its body to her hand with cloth and extract that one with equality, because it will soon be forgotten.
When the fetus is born on its feet, then accordingly you should push those inwards, and accordingly turn the fetus little by little, and accordingly bring one foot of it and stretch those little by little.
But when they are born into the arms, then accordingly you should command her to expel, and make that one sneeze with conditions, because it will soon be forgotten if God so wills.
And if it is not forgotten according to what we have recounted, then accordingly you should return the fetus little by little until it pauses in its natural figure, because it will soon be forgotten with a lighter delivery.
And if it is prohibited according to all that we have recounted, then accordingly take mummy of alta and dissolved gum, and strike the whole in the mortar with good striking, and accordingly line up with water the woman's menses, at the lowest part of her belly. And accordingly make that one cease in hot water, until it achieves the hypochondria.
And when the parts below are relaxed, then accordingly make her take a sub-fumigation of myrtle and pause that one for her. And when she has taken the sub-fumigation for an hour, then accordingly make her lie on a pillow, and accordingly make that one sneeze and stretch out her mouth, and take away from that, and press the lower part of her belly with light compression, because the fetus will soon be forgotten.
Delivery of the Fetus Lying Transverse with One of Its Hands Hanging Down. Be gentle in reducing the woman's hand, but if you cannot reduce that one, then accordingly lift the woman and make her walk.
And if she cannot walk, then accordingly make her lie on the bed, and conceive the woman's arms with a violent concussion, and accordingly administer those remedies which you and we have recounted from mummy.
And if the childbirth is over, then accordingly make her lie on a pillow, and accordingly study the reduction of the hand, and bring forth the fetus according to natural figure, and make the woman sneeze and command her to compress herself until it is forgotten.
Delivery of the Fetus with its hands spread out and the woman's flesh on both sides of her mother. It is necessary that the midwife hold the hand of the fetus and accordingly turn it little by little, and make it easy for that one.
And when it is equalized, and accordingly pause on the menses of that one with what we have recounted from oils and mummy.
And accordingly command her to cough little by little, and when you have finished that, then accordingly make her lie on a pillow and command her to incline herself over the right side, and accordingly command her to be compressed; and make that one sneeze with conditions. Exit of the Prepared Fetus Above the Side.
When the child is born in a terrifying manner according to this method, consider, and accordingly you should insert the second finger with your nail into that one until it is evacuated of humidity.
And if the fetus is suspended over the face and neck of her, then accordingly you should insert that one from the umbilicus, so that it may not be retained and die.
And accordingly push the fetus into the lower parts until it pauses according to what is necessary, and command the woman to compress herself several times, and if God so wills, it will be forgotten with a lighter delivery.
Exit of Twins or Many Fetuses. Know that twins are often born in sets of two or three, and sometimes even four, but this is rare and should not happen; but there are causes that are against nature, and do not live.
And in those cases, whether they are multiple or not, one second fetus, and they are separated by ciphac, distinguish those into the ligament at the umbilicus of each of them. And sometimes they are forgotten like this, as if it were one fetus for a lighter delivery, and sometimes they are delivered non-naturally like we have recounted.
And if some of them are difficult to deliver and proceed according to what we have said about the non-natural figures, then accordingly you should care for those like we have recounted.
And if the midwife is subtle and does that which facilitates ease and subtlety, and with delay, and is gentle according to all figure, as it is prepared from the beginning leading to health.
Remembrance of what is formed in the womb from embryos and aborted fetuses.
Some women are formed in the womb to have one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and even ten children, and you should verify that a woman aborts nine times and another has all ten, which is caused by the measurement of the wise sages.
And all this is necessary in the science of the midwife, for it is a great deal that appears like this to her, and therefore pause should be made at this point with what is necessary.
Chapter 76.
On the extraction of the fetus when it is dead.
When you care for the dead fetus with what we have said in the division of medicine and it is not born outside, and you are forced to use an operation on her, then accordingly it is necessary that you consider whether the woman has a healthy virtue and is not affected by any of the accidents by which on her there is feared loss.
Then accordingly it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back on a bed or pillow, and her head be inclined downward and her arms elevated.
And the minister should hold that one by two parts or tie her in a bed for so that the body of hers does not extend too far during the extraction of the fetus.
And accordingly you should moisten the mouth of her womb with olive oil and mummy of alta and fenugreek and seed of lily.
And accordingly the midwife should take her hand with those oils and mummy, and accordingly insert her hand with ease into the womb, and accordingly search for the location where the fingers will be placed on the fetus.
And when you have found the convenient location: then accordingly you should consider if the fetus is prepared to come out on its head, and accordingly place your fingers in the hollow of the skull, or in the neck, or in the mouth, or on the palate, or below the beard, or in the furcula of the skull, or in the places proper for the ribs, or below the hypochondria.
But if the delivery is over the feet of hers, then accordingly in the pelvis or in the middle of the ribs.
And accordingly you should hold the fingers with your right hand, and pause the curvature of hers in that location which is between the said fingers of your left hand, and insert your hand with ease and place the fingers in one of those locations which we have said, until you reach the cause of birth.
And accordingly you should pause and remain in the position of hers another finger, or the third if it is necessary, in order that there may be a gentle attraction, and not an extension according to her natural straightness only.
And it is good for all parts, in order that the delivery of hers may be facilitated as if it were done by hand.
And it is good in her that which is between them, so that the extension may be softened; and if some part of hers is retained, then accordingly the midwife should apply some of her said fingers with oil and insert those expertly and turn around with what is retained.
Therefore if the part of the fetus is forgotten, then accordingly the fingers should be permitted to enter that location which is higher up; and make it so until all the fetus is brought forth.
But if the hand is stuck in front of the other, and it is not possible to reduce that one by the constriction of hers, then accordingly it is necessary that cloth be wrapped around that one; and accordingly extract that one until all is brought forth, and insert it either at the joint of the hand or in the elbow.
And so it is necessary to do the same in the other hand and in both feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or if there is constriction during the delivery, or if there is water adjusted in the head of hers, then accordingly it is necessary to insert between the said spiny spatula and make an incision on the head and extract the water, or what discloses that one with a tool which is called "alundat", whose form will come with the forms of other instruments in the capital chapter which is apropos to this.
And similarly do the same if the fetus is naturally large-headed: and accordingly it is necessary to incise that one with an allegator, or take that one with an alundat as we have said; and accordingly extract the bones with forceps.
And if the head is extracted and is constricted at the furcula, then accordingly it should be incised in order that the humidity which is in the feet may be poured out.
But if it is not complicated nor obedient to delivery, then accordingly you should incise the head as soon as possible according to what will be possible for you.
And if the afterbirth is apostematic or is in water retention, then accordingly it is necessary that you perforate that one until the humidity which is in hers flows out.
But if the fetus is on her feet, then accordingly the attraction of hers is light and the direction to her mouth is light.
But if it is constricted by the belly and feet, then accordingly it is necessary that you extract that one with cloth which you will have wrapped around your hand, and that you incise the belly and feet until the water which is in those flows out.
But if the other members are stuck and return to the head, then accordingly insert your left hand; but if the mouth of hers is swollen, then accordingly insert your hand into the prepuce of her, and search for that one's head, and attract it with those fingers until it enters into the mouth of hers, and accordingly insert one or two fingers and draw hers towards those.
And if the mouth of hers is constricted by apostematic swelling which occurs in her, then accordingly it is not necessary to trouble about that; but before administering effusion of humid and greasy causes. And administer poultices; and follow the patient in waters that soften and moisten.
And if the fetus is on her ribcage, then accordingly it should be, if possible, sewn; and administered water as we have said in the live fetus.
And if this is not possible, then accordingly it should be incised in pieces, and extracted.
And accordingly one should not leave any cause behind the second finger.
And when you have completed all your operation, then accordingly administer the water as we have said for curing of apostematic swellings which occur in her.
And if there occurs a flow of blood, then accordingly send it down in stiptic waters and administer the other cure.
And you have already seen a woman whose womb was dead, and accordingly on that same spot another pregnancy was undertaken, and accordingly the fetus is another. It happened to her that after a long time an apostema occurred in her umbilicus; and it swelled up into a boil, and began to burst forth.
And you were called to her cure, and treated her for a long time, and the wound did not consolidate.
Then you applied some causes of strong attraction to her, and extracted one bone from her, and accordingly passed some days, and extracted another bone; and you were too amazed, since in the womb there was no bone.
And then you thought that they were the bones of the dead fetus.
Therefore you covered the wound, and extracted many bones from her, the woman existing in her own millenary dispositions, and already living in such a manner for a long time, and corrected herself with a small piece of flesh.
And you did not hesitate to say that it was strange, but rather because in this is science and aid to what the physician has with his hand for curing.
Of the forms of instruments which are necessary for extracting the fetus.
The shape of the vice in which the mother is opened.
This is the shape of a strengthener in which the free ends are joined together by two vice-like contraptions at both extremities of two feet. And however this vice should be more subtle than the strictor, and made of ebony or boxwood.
And the diameter of each stick is two fingers and a little more, and the margin of each is one finger, and the length of each is one palm and a half; and in the middle location of two sticks are two adjustments of those sticks which are already fixed, the length of which is half a palm and a little more, and the diameter of each is two fingers or a little more.
And these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the mother so that they can be opened with those when you turn the two prescribed vice-like contraptions.
Another similar form, more subtle and lighter:
It should be made of ebony or boxwood according to the shape of forceps. However, at the end of it there are two additional pieces like those, and the length of those additional pieces is one palm, and the diameter of each is two fingers.
And when you want to open the mother with those, then accordingly you should cause the woman to lean back on her bed, with her feet hanging down, and open what is between her thighs. And accordingly place your hand with the instrument as you would with forceps, in equal measure according to the quantity that you want of the appreciation of the mouth of the mother, until she does what you want.
The form of vice which the ancients called:
Form of impeller, with which the fetus is impelled.
Form of Amisidate, with which the great head is contained.
And it is assembled to forceps which have teeth at the end, just like times, and some times are made long just like forceps according to this form, just like times, with teeth just like the teeth of a saw blade into which it is inserted and contained. Form of Amisidate little:
Form of finger having a spine:
Form of finger having two spines:
Form of spatula having two extremities with which the head is cut off.
Form of two broad spatulas:
All those instruments are exercised, and when more species of that and prepared by the artisans, as much as it is lighter for their operation and more numerous are the people for their quantity.
And you must not omit to prepare those instruments, whatever they may be, because the necessity of them is not excusable.
Of the extraction of the second finger.
When the second finger is retained, you must command the child to retain its right hand, and accordingly make her sneeze with conditions, and strengthen your hand on the mouth of hers and on her nostrils, and if by so it has emerged outside, it is good.
And if not, then accordingly take a ball and pierce a hole in the cover, pause in that herb and fill the mouth of the mother with it, just like with celandine and rue and anise and chamomile and Arabic senna and cassia lignea and safflower. All these herbs or some of them are submerged in water in the ball, and pause it on the fire.
And accordingly place a cane from flax in the mouth of the mother, and hold it until the vapor comes out into the concavity of the mother.
And accordingly make her sneeze just as we have said, and the second finger will be expelled with speed.
But if this cure does not work and the second finger remains, then accordingly command the midwife to submerge her left hand in sesame oil or in a mixture of altarion, and accordingly insert that into the conic cavity and search for the second finger, and when you have found it, then take it and stretch it little by little. But if it is annexed to the womb of the mother, then accordingly insert your hand according to what we have recounted, and when you have found the second finger, extract it little by little according to the rule, so that the mother does not suffer from excessive attraction. And accordingly it should be facilitated on both right and left sides with ease.
And if the mouth of the mother is constricted, as we have already recounted the cure with sneezing and medication from the ball with herbs.
But if it is not expelled with all the causes which we have recounted, then accordingly take heed that you do not force it upon her in iteration of abstraction, but rather it should be brought to the mouth of the mother and placed at the cleft of the woman, and accordingly make it crusty with egg white and tetra-pharmacum; for that will cause it to rot away after a few days and be dissolved.
But when it rots away, it rises to the head, and to the stomach, and leads the patient astray; and accordingly it is necessary that sub-fumigations and conveniences are administered accordingly.
But some of the Ancients have already experimented with sub-fumigation of Nazitort and dried figs.
Form of instrument with which the woman is sub-fumigated for the retention of menses and the second finger:
It should be made of beryl or horn.
And it should be paused with the subtle extremity in the cavity and the broad extremity above the fire, and the sub-fumigation should be paused on the arms of the fire.
And hold that in until the sub-fumigation is consumed and iterate another one.
Of the cure for the unbroken navel of the child.
Many children are born with navels that are not perforated, those which have already become subtle and opaque. Then accordingly instruct the midwife to pierce that navel with her finger; and if not, then pierce it with a sharp spatula, and be careful not to touch the liver.
And accordingly pause on that navel, pouring in wine and oil; and accordingly cure it with egg white until it is clean.
But if you fear that it may become opaque, then accordingly pause a tube in the navel for several days, and stop when the child wants to pass stool.
And if the navel becomes opaque due to consolidation of wound or aposteme; then accordingly it should be incised, and accordingly cured with the water which we have said for the cure and the lead.
Of the cure for fistulas that remain behind.
The fistulas that remain in the departure, which are lower than the navel and thicker, those which remain near the anus outside or in the space of one side.
And it is a single fistula or multiple ones.
And when that nodule is ancient and flows with white watery fluid or subtle pus, and some times it has some of these fistulas penetrating.
And those penetrating ones are known by what comes out of them through excretion and windiness; and sometimes the patient uses the method of excretion, and very little is expelled from those worms.
And some of those fistulas penetrate into the space, entering the bladder and the urethra; and some of those penetrating ones enter the junction of the cleft and the notch of the clitoris.
And the way to know if a penetrating fistula is not penetrating is that you insert your finger into the anus and gently probe with a subtle instrument of horn or iron in the fistula when there is no resistance.
But if there is resistance in that, then accordingly insert into it a subtle instrument of lead or horsehair until you feel the instrument or hair in your finger.
And if you don't feel it at all nor proceed from the tube any cause of emission or worm or windiness, just as we have said, then accordingly know that it is not penetrating, and accordingly give up the cure.
And when the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or urethra, then accordingly its significance is evident from the urine of that and prohibition of it to be so, in order that the place may be consolidated with medicine.
But if it is penetrating into the junction of the cleft or into the bone and causing pain in the circuit, then accordingly its sign is that the instrument will pass through here if there is no resistance in the bone, and causing pain in the circuit of the departure; and that from there you will have pus always; and that it will not be cured by medicine, nor consolidated with egg white.
And in all those penetrating fistulas there is no complete cure, and the cure of those is labor and toil of skilled physicians on which we have fixed.
But in that which is not penetrating and not ancient, expectation of healing with iron is hoped for according to what we have recounted, and what has already been proved.
And so the patient lies between your two hands and raises their knees to theirs, the clefts being inclined towards the belly of the patient, and accordingly insert a lead or horn instrument into the fistula if there is resistance, until you know the place where the instrument can pass.
And if the patient feels pain around the navel, then accordingly you should insert your finger into the navel.
And if you feel the instrument already having passed through and beginning to penetrate, or if you feel between your finger and that siphac or flesh, then accordingly you know for certain that it is penetrating; and then do not labor on that, since there is no healing in that, just as we have said.
But however, some say that it can be cured in certain men.
And the medicine by which it is hoped for recovery in that is that you burn a subtle cauter, according to the size of the fistula, just as we have said before, and insert that ignited into the fistula until it spreads around the navel; and accordingly repeat that two or three times until you know that all those adjusted flesh-tubes are fixed, which resemble the feathers of an owl.
And accordingly cure that with calomel wraps wrapped in parchment, until all those adjusted flesh-tubes are cleansed; and accordingly cure that with medicines that generate and consolidate the flesh, and if it is healed, good is; and otherwise, it will not be healed at any time by other treatment.
And if the instrument enters and does not penetrate into the navel which is in the anus, and between that and the instrument which is a velamen of flesh or ciphac, and sometimes the fistula opens in what appears to be the surface of the skin, then accordingly dry the skin from the beginning of the fistula, and you will see it drying with the instrument, and it will be in the fistula until the drying reaches the location where the extremity of the instrument is, and through the instrument is liberated and cut.
And accordingly cleanse those flesh-tubes which are assembled like the feathers of an owl, and do not remain any cause.
But if a flux of blood comes out sometimes when you are cleaning those flesh-tubes, then accordingly take the milk that is and of the pus, it is to cauterize with fire or acute medicine, for cauterizing with fire adjusts two good habits: first, adjustment of those adjusted flesh-tubes, and secondly, abscission of the blood from excessive humidity.
And accordingly cure that with calomel wraps wrapped in parchment or in threefold cloth until the wound gets better, and accordingly cure the wound with egg white, hard flesh generating and consolidating.
And thus medicines in which there is astringency and excess; when accordingly it is restored, it is already healed and you do not fear iteration.
But if the fistula has already penetrated into the cavity of the anus and is prolonged from the surface of the body, then accordingly insert your finger into the anus and investigate with it.
And thus if you find the instrument and between you and it is a velamen of ciphac or flesh, and it is intended for penetration, then accordingly there will be no operation in that place, but only according to the way of faith and hope.
Which cause is to be administered in one of three ways: either to cauterize that as we have said; or to dry it until you achieve the conquest of it so that it becomes possible for you to insert the instruments and the cure intended; and not proceed with drying at all because you do not want to excise the liver containing the navel, and the patient's wish is to come true; and accordingly cure that with what we have said, since it will be healed very quickly; or to lengthen that velamen and clean up that pus that dries out that area into the proper anus, as we have said, either with a probe or another sharp instrument of sharp extremity, and accordingly cleanse those flesh-tubes which are in the section until you can see through it; and accordingly strive to make the restoration of all the wound with drying, and if the upper opening is not consolidated, and the fistula remains open in the departure of the anus, and becomes easier for the patient. And sometimes the fistula is ended according to this manner: when you insert the instrument into the fistula, and it is in the lateral part of the anus around the surface of the body with the skin and on the margin of the anus, then take hold of the perforated extremity, which is like a needle prepared for sewing according to this form:
and insert it into that faithful wrap of five folds or around those, and accordingly insert the instrument with faith into the fistula until you achieve the conquest of it.
But if it is penetrating in the margin of the anus, then accordingly you extract the thread from that tube and insert your finger into the anus; and extract the extremity of the thread and adjust the two ends together, and strengthen each one, and leave it like that for a day or two, and when more the thread is inserted into the flesh, strengthen it until those flesh-tubes are extracted which are between the two ends of the thread and fall.
And accordingly cure the wound until it is consolidated and healed.
But if the orifice of the fistula is not penetrating, then accordingly make it penetrate in whatever way you are prepared, but not in the cavity, for it is not up to you to do that lest you excise the liver; and accordingly do that until it is healed.
The form of the spatula spine with which the fistula is opened: its curvature is very sharp and the other part is non-sharp, so that you do not excise anything that is not necessary, just as sometimes.
Of the suturing of hemorrhoids in which blood flows during the incision of those.
Hemorrhoids are according to two manners, for either they are between the anus resembling charcoal, or else those are like a bunch of raisins. And those are small and large, and the blood flows from them constantly and is one, or many, and outside the anus, and in the extremities of it.
But however, those that are outside the anus are according to the measures of little moisture, from which citrine water or a small amount of blood with continuous flesh flows, and according to the color of the flesh.
And the cure for that which is outside the anus is to command the patient to settle down and to express themselves into the anus until it opens and the hemorrhoids appear before you. Then you take hold of it and suspend with the hooks or whatever instruments you have at your disposal, and accordingly cut away those hemorrhoids along their roots.
But if the hooks are not taken in those because of their moisture and softening, then accordingly take those with a rough cloth or with a piece of cloth or with a woolen rag, and extract them with your fingers, and accordingly cut away those hemorrhoids and powder some powders over them around the incision, so that they become attached to those at the place of cauterization; or cauterize those according to what is precedented in the chapter on cauterizing. And accordingly cure those with another cure until they are healed.
And if the anus does not obey evacuation, then accordingly anoint the patient with anointing oil in which there is a small biting, and wash it with that water that is in the anus and make it obey evacuation slightly when the patient has evacuated.
But if the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, then accordingly the cause of their being is easy, and it is that you take those with your finger or with hooks, and cut away those, and accordingly cure those with water as we have said until they are healed.
And whoever will make incision, must administer suturing of them according to this manner: take a thread wrapped and insert that into the needle and accordingly extract the hemorrhoids at the upper parts, and make it penetrate through the root of the other part, and envelop the two ends of the thread in the most distant part of the needle, and so laterally; and strengthen the hemorrhoid with strong suturing, and accordingly tie off the thread and extract the needle.
And do this to all of them, and leave one and not cut it off, in order that the superfluity of blood may flow from that.
And accordingly place a cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote on the anus, and place that over it and command the patient to rest. And accordingly leave it until it is closed; and when it is closed, cure those with egg whites or another cure until it is healed.
And since they are so ancient and do not respond to that medicine, then accordingly you must cut away those parts with the point of a spatula or your finger until they become moist and the excess flesh above is absorbed by those, which prevents consolidation; and accordingly cure those until they are consolidated.
Then accordingly you must cut away those parts with a reason more violent than the first one, until they bleed and are excoriated; and accordingly cure those until they are healed.
Know that Almesamar is the key, and it is not so if not according to the color of the flesh like a cap of chivalry, and it is made throughout the body and especially in the parts below the feet and those said above, and thus one must use force by means of those pains to drive away love.
And then it is necessary to incise that which is in the cavity of the key, and to keep it with forceps or hooks, and to eradicate its root; and accordingly cure that.
And if you wish, cauterize it according to what is preceded in the chapter on cauterizing.
But truly, warts are small, hard, round nodules on the surface of the skin, and many times they appear on children's faces.
And the cure for it is to stretch and incise that, or to strengthen that with a thread or skin until it closes. And if you wish, cauterize it, according to what we have said, with fire or acute medicine.
But a mole is a small, fatty or fistulous prominence on the surface of the skin that becomes inflamed when it is attacked by the fire and appears to be mummified around the body.
And the cure for it is that you take a needle of goose quill or of vulture's feather, and make it strong, and place that on the mole so that it contains the circle of the needle in the parts of the skin; and accordingly revolve your hand with the needle until you incise what is in the circuit of the mole, and place it in the flesh of the skin, and eradicate the mole from its root.
And if you wish, do this with a needle or iron according to this form:
Be the upper part of the needle very thin, soft (it is not perforated), wrapped so that on the said surface it learns to be ablated and the revolution of that.
And if you wish, cauterize the mole according to what is said before in the chapter on cauterizing in the book of medicine.
The form of the instruments that are administered to give anointing.
Sometimes it is made anointing of silver or lead or melted iron or hammered iron; and sometimes it is made with small instruments big or small according to those which are administered, for that which is administered to the little children is small; and of those whose bottoms are rough or wrinkled, the anointings of those are small.
The form of great and little anointing.
The head of the needle above, in which the pouch is attached, should be wide according to this manner; and there should be a distinction at the point where the pouch is attached, just as it is sometimes.
And the extremity of it below, which is inserted into the anus, should be soft (not open) like a lion's, going back to subtlety; and on one side of it there are two holes, and on the other side one hole, and the width of the hole according to the thickness of the rays and thicker by a little.
And the pouch in which medicines from the bladder of an animal or wool of a sheep are placed, and the root of it is one palm.
And it should be pierced by many small holes like it is turned around; and if the space which is between the holes is as thick as said.
And accordingly insert it into those holes a strong thread of raw thread which is of ten threads or surrounds them; and adjust the pouch to that, and when the pouch is placed in it, be tight at the head of the anointing between two distinct ones with strong constriction, and accordingly anoint each hole: But the quality of anointing with that is that you fill the pouch with medicine, which should be warmed according to the quantity of the tolerance of the patient; and beware that it is not too hot nor too cold.
And accordingly, the patient should be placed on their back with their legs elevated and a cloth spread under them, and pause below it one cushion or a bolster; and accordingly anoint the extremity of the cauterizer with oil or albumen of hen or mucilage of fenugreek or similar substances; and accordingly insert that into the anus with ease, and accordingly the attendant takes the pouch and evacuates that with two hands and samples with violence until everything in the anointing is evacuated into the bedpan; and accordingly extract the anointing and the patient raises their legs to the wall.
And if the medicine forces that to happen, keep it as long as possible; and if they sleep with that for all one night, it is more likely to be a remedy.
But if you anoint that in the diseases of flux of the stomach and the evacuation of it is obstructed, then accordingly you will iterate the cauterizer until it is healed.
And if there are hemorrhoids or apostemes in the anus, then accordingly use a cauterizer that is very subtle and lion-like, from those cauterizers with which children are anointed.
The treatment of wounds.
And I have already said in the division of the treatment of wounds that which is fitting for a free person, and I say thus the treatment of those with me and with medicines according to their complement.
Therefore I say that wounds are diversified according to this, inasmuch as they are made the wounds and according to the place on which they are placed.
And the causes by which many times wounds are made are as follows: like a blow of a hammer, or incision with a sword or dagger, or percussion with a lance, or with a staff, or with an arrow, or similar to those of many other causes.
But the wounds that are on the parts of the body are as follows: like a wound that is on the head, or neck, or arms, or belly, or thigh, and similar to those of the limbs.
And I recommend the treatment of some wounds by which one pauses that rationalization and rule over other wounds.
And I begin with the wounds of the head, simple ones, for the recollection of the complex ones will come at the beginning of the fourth chapter.
Therefore I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head and is not a fracture, then consider: if it is caused by a blow of a hammer or something similar, and already the bone has been so broken that there is great swelling and you fear that an apostema may form, then you take hold of the patient's head and fleubotomize it as soon as possible, without delay; and extract from that wound as much blood as is necessary according to the quantity of the virtue of the medicine, unless there is some other cause prohibiting fleubotomy, especially if the blood that has issued from the wound is little.
And be the fleubotomy on the opposite side of the wounded part; and beware the patient of replenishment, and of wine and of heavy foods.
But if some cause prohibits from the beginning, then accordingly minimize the food and do not approach meat or wine.
And pause over the wound if an apostema has formed cautiously, and cut in with rosy oil or wine that is stipticated.
But if it is certain of an apostema cautiously, then accordingly pause over the wound, if it is recent and its air has not changed that powder which I recommend in small quantity.
And if the air has already changed that, then accordingly pause over another application until it is healed.
But if the wound is great or caused by incision with a sword and similar things, and the lips of it are not adjusted for pulps, then accordingly adjust those with suture according to what I recommend about the suture of wounds.
But if the wound is already discovered to be of bone and flesh, and there is no retention of it except a small suspensori, then accordingly incise that and accordingly cure the wound with medicines and restore the flesh in its place, and command the patient to abstain from foods which are gross: heads and forms, similar to theirs, until it is composed.
And if you find in the bone putrefaction and it does not adhere to the bone, then accordingly incise all that is rotten and take out what remains, and accordingly cure what remains.
But if in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood flux can occur, and it is not abscessed by medicines, then accordingly inquire about the artery, and if you find that it is not incised, then accordingly incise it with a spatula or tie it off; and if necessary, provoke what we have said to not concur, then accordingly cauterize until the blood is absorbed.
And if these wounds are simple and small, then accordingly the cause of them is light; in such a way that you powderize on those this powder, for it consolidates before the air changes those.
And the manner of the powder is this: take one part of olive oil, two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of non-extinguished cause; all well mixed and crushed, and fill the wound with it, and construe it with good constriction until it adheres well to that, and coagulates with the blood.
And accordingly strengthen that above with poultices and compress it, and do not remove it until it is thus as if it were not apostemed, for the medicine is not eradicated from it until it is healed.
And sometimes do this alone, when you don't have in front of you olive oil and dragon's blood.
And already perform this same operation on great wounds when it is necessary to pause over them and be tight, and on recent wounds with their own blood, which the air has not altered.
And if the air has altered them, and especially when it is in the time of summer, then accordingly do not think about the position of this powder, but instead cure those with what we have said, in such a way that you pause over them with certain ointments or with powders made from flour and water mixed with honey until they take on a purulent appearance; and accordingly cure those with another cure until they are healed.
But if there is a fracture in the bone of the wound, and it is small, then accordingly extract what remains with gentle gestures.
And I will say the cure for fractures of the head in this which is poisonous.
Of wounds of the neck.
But if the wound occurs in the neck, then accordingly there is no difference in medicine and between the wound of the head when it is simple.
But if the nerves of the neck are cut or an artery is injured, then accordingly if it is a nerve, do not intervene with surgery but rather avoid any cure that would cause violent stiptication, such as zinnier and zegi which is vinegar and similar to theirs, because they are injurious to nerves and contract them. And do not pause over the wound any cause of total numbness, for the substance of nerves is numb and their continuation is in the brain, which is the most noble part of all limbs.
And if you use what is cured with light medicines, such as it being washed with lukewarm water, some times injected into rose-colored or non-rose-colored oil, and then when it is washed with lukewarm water and the other parts are minored according to this manner, and ointments moistened.
But if the wound is great, then accordingly administer suture, or bind the lips of it, and accordingly cure that with poultices until it is healed.
But if the wound is deep or occurs in the lowest part of purulent matter, then accordingly pierce that in the most depressed location.
But if in the wound an artery has been incised and a flux of blood has resulted, then accordingly separate or dry that, or tie off that, or cauterize that if necessary provokes at that.
But if the vertebrae of the spine or all have been incised and the veins of the neck are saved, then accordingly adjust the lips of the bone with suture over the canal of the spine and do not touch that; before equaling that and reducing it to its natural figure, and accordingly strengthen that with decent stricture, and leave it for a few days; and accordingly cure that with ointments in which there is stiptication and excitement until it is healed.
But if the wound is in the bone and has made an impression, then accordingly puncture that, and if there are fragments of bone in it, extract all those that you can from them; and what is not clothed, leave that until the wound is purulent, and separate and be relieved from the excrescence.
And if the wound is recent, then accordingly powderize on it the powder which I have recommended to you. But if in the wound there is a fistula, then accordingly cure that with what will be remembered in its own chapter.
If it is a lance or dagger wound and the depth of the wound is considerable, then accordingly consider whether the patient has ventilation when they are lying down; accordingly know that the wound is mortal.
And if the wound is not deep and the wound is recent with its own blood, then accordingly pause in it on the first hour with powder, and do not strengthen that so that the blood is not retained in the depth of the wound and returns to the heart and harms the patient; but rather pause in it with an attractive ointment, and remove it two times a day.
And if the ointment is not present, then accordingly pause in the orifice of the wound with a piece of cloth so that it sucks out what you have from the humors; and make the patient sleep over the wound so that the fluid that is there will be adjusted.
But if three days or more have passed since the wound and the patient does not experience spasms, tremors of the heart, nor constriction of the armpits, and has other good dispositions towards it, then accordingly know that the wound is healed; and then cure that with poultices and another cure until it is fully healed.
But if the healing of it is impeded and it has been open for a long time, then accordingly know that it has become a fistula; cure then that according to its own chapter.
And if the wound is caused by incision of a sword or dagger and is simple in the surface of the foot or head, then accordingly cure that with what precedes suture, if it is great, or with powder, if it is small.
But if the wound has made an impression in the bone and there are pieces of bone that need to be extracted, then accordingly twist the wound and cut to extract those pieces, if they are separated. But if they are not separated, then accordingly leave them inside until the wound purifies, and the extraction of them is relieved.
And for the other wounds that occur in the other members, the treatment in healing is the same as what we have said.
Of Wounds of the Belly.
The indisposition which occurs in the belly is either great, or small, or middling.
And small disruption is made difficult by another manner, and it seems that the reduction of theirs is more difficult if you do not take care to introduce their substance into its place at once, for it opens up and becomes swollen, making it difficult for the instrument to be used.
And therefore the best disruption is middling, for in that there is not difficulty in reducing the budel, just as it is difficult in the two species mentioned before.
And know that suturing the belly is according to four manners, but two sutures are common which are necessary for suturing other wounds of the body.
And two other sutures proper to it communicate with the other wounds, but are more proper in the suturing of the belly.
And I recommend to you whatever exposition and declaration.
Therefore I say that when the wound is small and there is some cause of the belly from it, and it is made difficult to reduce it, then accordingly this is in one of two ways: or by the smallness of the disruption as we have said, or when the belly has come inflated due to the coldness of the air.
And therefore when this is so, accordingly it is necessary that you scrape that in such a way that you submerge a sponge or damp cloth in hot water alone, or that you gather in warm water, and cyperum, and spic, and then apply that to the belly until the inflation is resolved.
And sometimes it does this with vinegar in which there is a purging quality, and it is better than hot water alone for the resolution of the inflation.
And therefore when you see the inflation be resolved, accordingly you moisten the belly with water in which is cooked alum and meadow-sweet, because through this the instrument of it is facilitated with little cause.
But if the instrument of it is excused in this cure, then accordingly you cut the disruption a little with an instrument by which they are incised and mortified.
And the first cure is better when it is proper and not severe, and there is no occupation to cut too much, nor to occupy oneself in cutting unnecessarily.
Of the Instrument: see how its shape is like this:
The one end of it bent and acute, and the other end not acute, and the extremity subtle, and not like the subtlety of a spatula, but rather blunt by a little.
And therefore when the wound is amplified and yields forth from the belly, accordingly it is necessary that its reduction be according to its natural shape, in its own proper place, if possible above all, for that is better.
But when the disruption is wide and is in the lower part of the belly, accordingly it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back, and place his knees higher than his head; and if it is in the upper part of the belly, then accordingly you place the head and legs higher than the remaining parts.
And similarly if the disruption is in one of the two parts of the belly, then accordingly place your intention and consideration always so that the part where the wound is may be higher than the other.
And thus it is necessary to administer this in great wounds and middling wounds.
And in small wounds, pause for that which is at your preparation, and accordingly make the minister be between your most skilled ones, who has the disruption entirely under his hand and adjusts the lips of it, and accordingly uncovers from this to that which sees some other cause for suturing.
And this is the common manner of suturing: take the needle, or count the needle according to the quantity of the amplitude of the wound; and accordingly leave it at the extremity of the disruption from the said ring finger, and strengthen the needle once, or twice, that you do not put faith in both ends of the bone, with both ends of the ciphac that is left the bone of the parties inwardly, until you make it penetrate from that part; and you have already added two ends of the bone and two ends of the ciphac, and so there are four orders.
And accordingly strengthen it with a double thread in the circle of the needle, and sometimes of two parts together, and accordingly add the two lips and the wound by decent addition; and accordingly leave the thickness of the finger and put another needle in it, and accordingly tie that with a thread like as it was tied to the first needle; and do not cease to do this if necessary with the needles until you have completed all the contraction of the wound.
And the needles should be middling between thickness and subtlety, for the thin needles barely cut into the flesh; and the thick ones are difficult to manipulate in the bone, and therefore it is necessary that they be middling in subtlety and thickness.
And it is not necessary that the needle be placed in both ends of the bone proper to one, lest the flesh be barely cut and the wound be inflamed before its consolidation.
And there should not be prolonged suturing so that the wound is prohibited from consolidation.
And accordingly insert the ends of the needles so that they do not disturb the patient during his sleep; and place poultices spread out on all sides, which have the ends of the needles; and leave those until you know that the wound is already consolidated.
And these species of suturing with needles in this manner are more convenient for small wounds, for they suffice in the suture of them with one needle or two or around those.
But the second suturing is common: and it is that you administer with suturing all four ends, of the bone and two ends of the ciphac, in one go, with a needle in which thread is wrapped evenly in subtlety and thickness.
And accordingly when you have the needle penetrated these four ends, withdraw the needle from that middle part of which it began, so that the thread retrays its place from the most superior part to the wound, so that the suturing be according to the suture of cloth with which the cloths are strengthened.
And pause between each suturing the quantity of the thickness of the finger smaller.
And this suturing is known to men.
And with such suturing I cured the wound which was inflicted on a man in his belly, which had been wounded by a dagger, and the disruption of the wound was greater than one palm, and it was situated around two palms from the middle of the belly, and the disruption was in the middle of the member; and then I reduced that after the belly had been open for 24 hours.
And the wound was consolidated in the space of 15 days or around, and I cured him and he was healed; and accordingly he lived for many years, and is converted to his former dispositions.
And other doctors had judged that he would not be healed; and by a miracle it was so, for you did not treat him with ointment, for it was in a place where ointment was not found nor any medicine, but you paused over the wound cutting twice a day and ablution with water of honey until he was healed.
But you said two species of proper suture according to the narrative of Paraula.
And it's that you began with the bone suture, and inserted the needle from the outside part to the inside part.
And therefore when the needle penetrates into the bone and meets the lacertus according to rightness and in length throughout the whole body, and leaves the end of the ciphac where you inserted the needle; and makes it penetrate into the other extremity the needle from the inside part to the outside part in the other extremity of the thigh.
And then when you have made it penetrate once, accordingly make it penetrate again in the same extremity of the thigh from the outside part to the inside part; and leave the end of the ciphac that is in this place, and make the needle penetrate into the other extremity of the inside part to the outside part.
And make it penetrate with that penetration of yours, by which you cause it to penetrate into the ciphac in the extremity of the mirror, which is on the part of it, until all that penetrates.
And accordingly begin from this side, and cut that with the end of the ciphac on the other side, and withdraw the needle from the bone which penetrated, and accordingly reduce it into that bone and close the end of the ciphac which is on the other side with this end of the mirror; and withdraw that one from the bone which is of part of it.
And make this once and another, and make this once again accordingly with the other once until you have closed all that is outside according to that example.
And the sum of this manner of suturing is that you close with suture of pellicies in which you close the skin, so that you close the ciphac one time from the part of the extremity of the bone, and then leave it once until you have completed all.
But the second species of proper suture which you said Gualia, and this is according to the word of him and by him recounted, is that you close it according to semilitut in which certain medicines are closed, so that they add all part to its corresponding part to what is convenient for nature; and apply the end of one side of it and the end of the mirror to the other end of it, and this is done according to how I have recommended.
And it is necessary that you put the needle into the end of the mirror at your own discretion from the outside part, and make it penetrate to the inside part in that same spot, and leave two ends of the ciphac; and accordingly revolve the needle and make it penetrate from outside to inside in two ends of the ciphac.
And accordingly revolve those threads, and make them penetrate from the inside part to the outside part in two ends of the mirror on the other side that is opposite.
And this manner of suture is better than the common light suture, and it is the suture of which I spoke earlier.
This is the word of Gualia

And if you feel pain or putrefaction in your own belly, since many times this is necessary, accordingly anoint that with black bean juice, and especially if the inflammation has been produced in the belly and is made an exit through the convolutions of it.

Of the cure of ulcers and fistulas.
Know that every wound and apostema when it becomes ulcerous and old, and is made an ulcer, and does not consolidate and always gets putrid, accordingly, in whatever member it may be, universally is called fistula and we call it that azuchem.
And fistula according to truth is a nodous formation, hard, white and painless, with which there is a convulsion similar to the pain of an owl; and for this reason we call that certain rizzats, i.e. pain.
And it is in some men humid, which gets putrid; and the humidity is very quickly absorbed in a few hours. And sometimes this humidity is great, and it is little, and it is thick, and it is subtle.
Already I have shown all those causes and their signs, as well as the cure of them with medicines in the division.
And it is necessary that you know how to make the cure of fistula, which is made by way of operation with my hands.
And know that fistula occurs in all the members of the body; because some are fistulas that penetrate to great veins and arteries, or to nerves, or to ciphac, or to belly, or to bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to some of the vertebrae of the back, or to some of the composite joints composed in such a way as from hand and foot; and those which are near to the proximity of the main member and similar.
And therefore that one of these fistulas which is according to this manner is one of the difficult-to-heal illnesses, and does not receive cure, and occupation with it is labor and ignorance.
And if some of the fistulas are of such depth that they do not penetrate to those places which I have mentioned, and you hope and trust in the cure of it, and wish to reach understanding of it, accordingly take a tenta of iron or steel, and if the fistula follows rightness, and you probe it with it.
But if the fistula is twisted, accordingly investigate it with a thin leaden tenta, because lead with the lightness of its own body is alleviated and curved by the twisting.
And if the fistula has many horrible things, it is not possible for you to signify on it with a tenta.
And accordingly close the opening through its openings, because the moisture which you use to cleanse it will flow into the other openings and run off from them.
And accordingly inquire exhaustively, according to which manner it is possible for you to know whether here there are bones or nerves, and if the fistula is long or short, or if it is a fistula with many openings and located above all on the sum of your strength, in your investigation, in which you investigate the patient, and the invention of pain due to your compression with your hand on the location, and similar signs and causes that occur at the apostema.
And when you have stood on all those causes with a steady gaze, accordingly go to the cure according to confidence: and it is that you consider whether it is an apparent fistula near or in a salient location, distant from the joint, or of nerves, or of artery, or of vein, or of one of the places which I tell you and say.
And accordingly you seal the fistula according to what is said before in the narration of it, and stop this that is in that filtration and corrupt flesh, and this that has been born from the orifice of the flesh, or of the tail and similar things, and cure this until it is healed.
But if the fistula is of long and deep depth, and it follows rightness, accordingly you must insert that into the preon as far as possible for you to signify; and accordingly clarify this from all its corrupt flesh; and accordingly administer certain wrapped medications, and introduce those into the convulsion of the fistula, which you have comprehended with iron.
And do this with that for several times until the acute medicine has consumed all that remains in the convulsion of the fistula from corruption.
And accordingly restore that with those which generate healthy flesh until it is healed.
But if it is not healed by this, accordingly you must cauterize that according to what we have recounted.
But if the cause of fistula is bone and it is necessary for you to certify this, accordingly you must inquire into that and seal that according to what we have recounted, unless you prohibit some cause of vein or nerve or main member as we have said.
But if the bone is discovered by you and there is some corruption and blackness in it, accordingly you must scrape out that entire corruption; and accordingly cure that with what encloses it until it is healed.
And if it is not healed and gets putrid as before, accordingly know that you have not succeeded in the complete eradication of corruption; and then you must uncover it again and make the reason of it and clarify it with the last remaining force of yours, and accordingly restore that.
And thus if it is healed, good it is; and otherwise, accordingly know that that corruption is in the deep, distant part of the body, which has not been reached, and then you must leave it alone.
And if the corrupted bone is small, or it is possible for you to draw that in, accordingly you must draw it with subtle forceps which are suitable for that.
And if there are many bones, accordingly make the extraction of all those in an exquisite manner, and leave not a single cause behind with your strength.
But if any cause of the humors makes you contrary, and in their insertion there is no fear nor error, accordingly insert those ligaments or flesh if it is here, and deliver the bones.
But if your preparation is not ready to extract the bones of your time, accordingly pause over the wound that perturbs the wound itself, and leave it until such time as this wound is in the environs of those bones, flesh, and ligaments, and guard the wound so that it is not consolidated, and the section which you have inserted into your operation be constricted.
They had, if you fear, pause over the wound submerged in a mixture of oil and wine, or a wound submerged in Egyptian balm, or in some of the green ointments, for when those ligaments rot, and the bones are separated from their ablation, and the attraction is alleviated.
But if it is a large bone like the bones of the hip or shoulder or similar to those, and what is corrupted from it is only the surface of it, accordingly scrape out that with a rasp only on the back side until that blackness and corruption is removed, and accordingly restore the wound.
But if what is corrupted from it is a great part, and the corruption has already reached the marrow of the bone, accordingly it is necessary to close that and insert it entirely into the place where the corruption has spread, and accordingly cure that until it is consolidated.
And I recommend to you this, that you persuade a man in his own way for you to pause and consider carefully about your operation.
There is a young man of about thirty years old, who suffers from pain in his hip, and the parts that are damaged on the outside are over the matter on the outside of the body until the matter has spread to the hip, and it is a material of apostema with great apostema, and there is no external cause.

And if the corruption is in the joint, scrape out that corrupted joint and cut the bone where it continues from the other part.

And know that what instruments and cuts are needed to cut into those bones are many according to the situation of the bones, their preparation, size, subtlety, greatness, smallness, hardness, and rarity; therefore, it is necessary for you to prepare all sorts of instruments suitable for each operation.
And know that this operation signifies to you about the type of instrument which you need; when with you is great study and long experience in the ways of this art, and witness to the manners of diseases, for accordingly you had already learned through your own observation what is suitable for each disease.
And accordingly, you have formed in the end of this chapter the number of instruments which I will pause with as simple ones, and with which I will proceed to your prohibition, which you will experience on others. **Forma de serra:**
**Forma de autra serra:**
**Forma de autra serra gran:**
**Forma de Ray:** **Sia le cap de aquest Ray segon la forma de cap de clau stellat, e les punts de lu sian segon la forma dels punts alstefegi.**
**E no conveneys sino que am aquel sian confricadatz les caps de las juncturas quan so corrumpudas, o es la boca gran ampla.**
**Forma de razori menor:**
**Forma de razori lat:**
**Forma de serra autra decentment fayta: sia fayt arc de lu pus sobira e la acuitat de lu de ferr, e le membre de lu de boys punhal descendant fayt.** **Forma de lu:**
**Forma de razori en la qual ha concavitat:**
**Forma de razori autra subtil:**
**Forma de autra razori de curvada extremitat:**
**Forma de rasori petit semblant a tenta:**
**Forma de inscisori autra minor:**
**Forma de un autra inscissori; aquest semblant a Ray, e la extremitat de lu es cum serra, e es exhibit en motz locs en la razio dels osses:**
**Forma de ray lo qual conveneys a rasio de aquel que es perforat dels osses:**
**E la extremitat de lu es triangulada e de aguda extremitat:**
**E es fayt de ferr de India, e semblantment cove que totas las causas que havem ditas de rasoris e de inscissoris e de serras.**
**De inscizio extremitatz e de la serratura dels osses.**
**Las extremitatz se poyresso o per causa intrinseca o per causa extrinseca, o cum tu auras medicat aquela corrupcio per curacio de aquelas medicinas e la curacio no comfereys, o vezes la corrupcio anar deves le membre la qual no percuteys denguna causa, lahoras cove que tu inscidas aquel membre entro aquo la hon acossec la corrupcio, per que le malaute evasesca per aquo de mort o de malicia que es major defeliment del membre.**
**E le senhal de aquel al qual accideys, es quel membre es fayt negre entro que sia cujat que foc la ja comburit, o se poyreys aprop la negror entro que la poyredura aquella ane entro aquel membre que siec lu e que prengua tot le cors; e donc coyta te am inscizio de aquel.**
**E semblantment si es causa de la corrupcio percussio de alcunes causas venenosas ayssi cum de scorpio mari o de vupera o de rutela e de semblantz.**
**E si la corrupcio o la percussio es en la extremitat del dit, lahoras tu inscideys le dit e no dones spazi a la corrupcion per que ane entro a la ma.**
**E semblantment si accedeys a la ma, lahoras tu inscideys aquela de la razit del focil, e no dones spazi a la corrupcion entro que prengua en le focil del bras.**
**E si envezeys aquel, lahoras inscideys le bras entro al coyde en la junctura.**
**E si passa otra la corrupcio e la vezes enviro le coyde, lahoras en aquel es la mort del malaute; e aministrar autra causa otra aquo en curacio es quantitat de vertut.**
**E semblantment fay del pe quando corrupcio envezeys le dit del pe, lahoras tu inscideys aquel entro ad un dels nozes.**
**E si pren en la pente del pe, lahoras tu inscideys tot le pe.** **Mays si pueja entro al denol, lahoras tu inscideys la camba entro a la junctura del denol.**
**E si la corrupcio ja es pervenguda sobre le denol, lahoras en lu no es engen sino dimissio, e layssar le malaute a la mort.**
**E la manieyra de inscidir le membre o de serrar lu es que tu strenhas le liament en la partida pus dejos la qual voles inscidir, e strenh autre liament sobre le loc; e extenda le ministre un liament a las partidas dejos, e extenda le ministra autra liament en sus; e tu separa la carn la qual es entre dos liamentz ain spatum lat entro que sia descuberta tota la carn; e aprop sia inscidit o serrat.**
**E cove que sia pausat drap de li de totas partidas per so que no toche le loc sa, e que vengua al malaute lesio ajustada e apostema caut.**
**Mays si accideys flux de sanc quando obras, lahoras tu cauteriza le loc coytadament, o pausa sus lu alcunas polveras restrenhentz le sanc; e aprop retorna a la tua medicacio entro que sia complida.**
**E aprop lia le membre plaguat am liament al u convenient, e cura aquel entro que sia sanat.**
**E yeu recomti a tu aquo que endevenc a un home en le sieu pe, aquest meteys accident le qual yeu e a tu recomtat, le qual es quar accidic a lu negror en le sieu pe am adustio that era asemblada a combustio de foc.**
**E aquela corrupcio accidic primiermente en le sieu dit entro que tendec tot le pe.**
**E adonc aquel home preparec per si meteys pus que vic la curacio anar al membre am la vehemencia de lu that atrobec de dolor e de adustrio de lu, e el inscidic aquel pe entro a la junctura, e foc sanat.**
**Lonc temps accidic a lu aquela meteys
**E adonc venc a mi, e so me perforsat repercutir aquela superfluitat am aquo that pausegui sobre la ma de las medicinas, aprop la mundificacio del cos de lu; e no es repercussa la superfluitat e comensec anar al autra dit entro que comensec en la ma.**
**E el apelec me a inscidir la ma de lu, e yeu no volgui far aquo sperant sobre la repercussio de aquela superfluitat, e mays que temegui deves la inscizio de la ma de lu mort, quar la vertut del malaute era sobre cazement.**
**E pus que el se desperec de mi, es retornat en la sua terra e pervenguec a mi que aquel home preparec e inscidic la sua ma tota, e es sanat.**
**E no he adhuzida aquesta narracio sino per que sia ajutori sobre aquo que catz de aquesta malautia, e que sia significacio per la qual sia significada e segon la qual sia obrat.**
**De cura sinuum et qualitate clisterizationis cum medicinis.**
**Quan accideys apostema en alcus membres carnozes el spazi de lapostema es prolonguat entro que fa colleccio de sania, e aprop es romput e perforat, e es eyssida de lu la sania, e roman le loc vuoyt quays cum si era vayssel, e la codena que es desobre lu ayssi cum drap subtiliat, e no es pervengut a deriera corrupcio, e no inprimeys en le os o en nervi ni en liament, es apelat sinu, e no es nompnat fistula.**
**Mays empero si le spazi es prolonguat entro que la corrupcio enprema en alcun membre, lahoras es appelada fistula e no zukem.**
**E la cura de lu es que inscidas aquela codena tota ayssi cum es revolvut, e majorment quan es subtiliada e es fayta cum drap, e comfizas que no adhereys al loc per la sua corrupcio.**
**Mays si tu speras that la codena adheresca e that aquela corrupcio no aya conseguit per deriera consecucio, e en la codena ha spassitut de cara, lahoras tu cura aquel am clisteri.**
**E es que consideras al sinu, e lahoras si es gran, el brac that yeys es de fetent odor, lahoras clisteriza aquel am medicament egipciac le qual es de oli e vi agre e ziniar recebent partidas enguals, e sian ajustadas en un vayssel, e sian coytas sobre le foc entro que'l medicament se fassa rog e pervengua a specitut de mel.**
**E aprop tu pren de lu aquo que es necessari e dissolveys lu am aygua e mel; e clisteriza am aquel le sinu, e strenh le orrifici de lu, e layssa la medicina en lu per la quantitat de doas horas.**
**E aprop extratz aquela am sprecio; e fay aquo per tantz dias entro que sia mundificat le sinu e sia remauguada la pudor.**
**E alcunas veguadas es clisterizat am aygua de cendre, quan no es a tu prezent aquest medicament; e es que tu prenguas la cendra de vitz, e met sobre lu aygua; e aprop cola aquela e clisteriza aquel am ela entro que te confizes quel sinu lahoras es ostat.**
**E si le malaute no ha tollerancia sobre le medicament egipciac ni laygua de la cendre, lahoras clisteriza aquel am aygua e mel e quays sia mesclat ziniar trissat, e clisteriza aquel am vi e mel mesclat, quar de proprietat de mel es que mondifique e lave, e le vi fa adherir le sinu, e majorment quan en le vi ha superfluitat de stipticitat e de siccitat.**
**E cum tu fas aquo alcunas veguadas e te comfizes quel sinu ja es remaugut, laoras clisteriza aquel am aquo que fa naysser la carn en lu.**
**E es that prenguas de enguent dyafinicon e dissolveys aquel am oli rozat e vi stiptic; o que clisterizas aquel am alcunas medicinas e enguentz others that hajan las proprietatz les quals ja he yeu scritz en le tractat dels enguents.**
**E si le orrifici del sinu es streyt en le qual no es recebuda la canula del clisteri, lahoras tu le amplifique aquel am ferr petit a petit, e pausa en lu calgua envolopada en enguent egipciac o en enguent basilicon entro que sia amplificat.**
**E semblantment si le orrifici es ample, laoras tu agregua las labias de lu am sutura e layssa de lu quantitat en la qual intre le clisteri ses addicio.**
**E si le orrifici de lu del qual corr le brac es elevat a las partidas desus, lahoras secca aquel en le pus bas loc que es en lu per que le brac corra entro dejos, quar quand le brac es coartat en la preondeza de sinu la carn esser en lu engendrada.**
**E si no es a tu possible seccar le sinu entro al enviro del os pus bas segon que voles, laoras te perforssa que prepares le membre am preparacio per la qual corr de lu le brac leugierament segon que es a tu apparelhat e que no sia en lu retengut alcuna causa del brac.**
**Mays aquel que es sobre le orrifici del sinu, le qual remauguas en tota hora per so que yesca aquo que es ajust en lu del brac.** **E per que sapias si aquo que corr de lu del brac es mot or pauc, o es digest, o es no-digest.**
**E am aysso tu considera le loc de aquel sinu, si en lu sent le pacient dolor o non, e si es en lu apostema.**
**E cum la tua medicacio es prolonguada en la tal manieyra, e vesas la matiera que es gitada sobre le orrifici del sinu ja adhereys, o se apropria adherencia, lahoras le mayti tu le deslia o le tertz dia, e quan deslias la plagua, lahoras muda le drap per autre e renova le enguent.**
**Mays si del sinu aprop lon spazi yeys virus subtil, lahoras no te desperes de la adherencia de li, quar la sanacio de lu se apropria, quar so alcus homes en les quals tarda generacio de carn en las lors plaguas, e de aquels so en les quals es fayt le contrari de lu.**
**E si del sinu aprop motz dias es yssit brac indigest, lahoras sapias quel sinu no adhereys; e si es tardada la adherencia del sinu e es la causa prolonguada, lahoras tu ajusta en exsiccacio de las medicinas, e si las medicinas so humidas en lor substancia e en la sua vertut, son seccas ayssi cum enguent dyafinicon, quan es en lu ajustada superfluitat de addicio de zegi.**
**E le mays derier am le qual es curat, es que prenguas de enguent dyafinicon e sia dissout en oli rozat, e sia sobre lu vojat vi antic engual en la sua substancia, e aprop comfeys aquel am lu, e usa de quello.**
**E ja fa semblant en aquela accio, quan no y a brac, enguent dyafinicon, mel quan es coyt entro que sia engrossat, e usa de lu; o que prenguas mirra e aloen e enses, e trissa tot e polveriza sobre le mel quando
**E alcunas veguadas so administratz am lu aristologia longua e razitz de lili celesti (e es lili celesti) e farina de errs e centaurea, e usa de aquels simples o ajustatz, trissa aquels e cribela e polveriza sobre le mel le qual he recomtat; e husa de lu.**
**E si es prolonguat le sinu, e no es sanat per aquesta curacio, lahoras sapias que la corrupcio es en le preon de lu, e ja fa enquisicio en les osses o en les autres membres durs o als liaments; lahoras tu le cura am curacio fistular, ayssi cum desus es dit.**
**De curacio de panarici et unguis attritae et incisione digiti additi et sectione.**
**Panarici es apostema le qual nays dejos la ungla del dit pous de la ma o del pe, e fort leu nays en les autres ditz, e cum es prolonguat e la sua curacio es mens prezada, o es apostemat de apostema caut, o es corrumput, e gieta brac entro que corrodeys la razitz de la ungla, e fort leu corromp aquela tota, e fort leu perve la sua corrupcio al os entro que es a lu odor fetent, e es fayta la extremitat del dit lada, e la color de lu es fayta fusca.**
**E donc quand tu auras aquel am aquo que havem dit en la divisio e no comfereys la tua curacio, lahoras cove que tu inscidas am ferr tota la superfluitat que es romasa de la ungla e aprop cauteriza la plagla aprop aquo, quar cauteri mot es juvatiu en aysso.**
**Mays si le os es sa e la ungla es sana, e las addiciones de la ugla vuoydas ja compren las carns a las partidas dedintz, e comensan lu punger e ledysso aquela, lahoras cove que tu pauses ray subtil dejos le angle de la ugla que pungeys la carn, e impelleys aquela sus e inscideys aquella carn am facilitat, e pausa sobre aquo que roman de la carn de las medicinas comburentz corrosivas entro que sia tot remaugut; e aprop cura aquel am enguentz entro que sia sanat.**
**Mays si la corrupcio ja enprem en le os, lahoras cove que tu inscidas le os aquel e le extraguas, car nul temps no es sanitation que sia en lu le os corrumput.**
**E si vezes la corrozio e la corupcio anar en le dit, lahoras tu inscideys aquel en un dels nozes segons que es premesa la sua rememoracio, e aprop cura aquel entro que sia sant.**
**Mays si a la ungla endeve percussio o atricio, e endeve en aquela dolor vehement, lahoras cove que tu al comensament fleubotomes le malaute, e aprop secca la ugla am spatum agut am seccio transversa desus en jus, e guarda te que la seccio no pervengua entro a la carn que es dejos la ugla, quar tu faras accidir al malaute dolor vehement, e sira causa a nativitat de la carn ajustada superflua en le loc; e aprop cura aquel loc am aquo que ceda dolor.**
**Mays dit ajustat, le quali es nat en las mas de alcus homes, fort leu es carnos tot, e fort leu so en lu osses, o fort leu es en lu ugla.**
**E alcus de lu son natz en la razit de la junctura, o es la nativitat de lu en alcus nozes dels ditz.** **Mays aquel que es nat en alcus nozes del dit no se mau, e aquest que es nat en las juncturas fort leu es maugut.**
**E de aqueles que son natz carnoses, la seccio es leugiera, e es que tu inscidas aquel deves la sua razitz am spatum lat.**
**Mays de aquel que es nat en la razitz de la junctura, la curacio es difficile; e donc guarda te de la abscizio de lu.**
**Mays en aquel que es nat en dit, deves les nozes, cove que tu inscidas al comensament la carn de lu am inscizio redonda entro al os, e aprop serra am una de aquelles serras convenientz ad aquo, e aprop cura aquel entro que sia sanat.**
**Mays consolidacio la qual accideys als ditz entre lor motas veguadas o per nativitat del home que nays enayssi, o per consolidacio de plagua o per combustio de foc, o per semblantz, adonc cove que secces aquella consolidacio entro que les ditz retorno a la sua forma natural.**
**E aprop pausa entre lor draps de li enfuzes en oli rozat per que no sian consolidatez leugierament, e separa entre aquels, o pausa entre aquels una lamina de plom subtil entro que sia consolidat segon que cove.**
**E semblantment si accideys consolidacio en alcus ditz am la palma, lahoras tu secca aquela consolidacio segon que es preparada e conveneys a la figura del membre.**
**De inscizio de vices, so son varicas.**
**Vices so son varicas, e so venas envolutas grossas plenas de superfluitatz melencolicas las quals veno en motz dels membres del cors, e le major adveniment de lor en las cambas, e majorment en las cambas dels itinerantz e dels laborantz e dels portantz.**
**Adonc cove que tu administres purgaio del cors de colera negra alcunas veguadas am expulcio fort, e aprop sangna le pacient de la vena basilica.**
**Mays la curacio de lor am ferr es segon dos manieyras: la una es que sia inscizas e sia atirat aquel sanc negre, e l'autra manieyra es que sia elevada la vena e sia extrayta tota.**
**La seccio de lu es segon aquesta manieyra: embroca al comensament la camba am aygua cauda mot entro que le sanc gros sia resolvut, que es feculent de la camba, e aprop strenh la camba del malaute a la partida pus sobirana de la coyssa entro a la partida dejos del denol am una benda, e aprop secca la vena en un loc, o en dos, o en tres am seccio ampla, e aprop eleva le sanc negra am la tieua ma de la partida dejos de la camba entro en sus, e desus en jus, entro que del sanc sia yssida la quantitat que voles e que veces habastar, e la qual tollera la vertut del malaute.**
**E aprop lia aquella, e comanda a lu que abstengua de las viandas colera negra engendrantz.**
**E itera la curacio per fleubotomia quan las venas so umplidas e aquo notz al malaute.**
**Mays la elevacio de lor es segon aquesta manieyra: tu que razas la camba del malaute, si en lu so motz pels, e aprop met le en banh e embroca la camba de lu am aygua cauda entro que senrogesesca e las venas sian exuberadas; o que sia exercitat per exercici fort, si banh no es a tu present, entro quel membre sia scalfat.**
**E aprop secsa la codena en le dreyt de la vena per seccio en le lonc o en le derier de lu deves le denol, o en le pus bas de lu deves lo talo.**
