**E aprop uobre la codena am uncis e excorja la vena de tota part entro que appara al sentiment, e es deves la appericio de lu que vezes aquella roga declinant a negror.**
**E donc cum evazeys e de la codena tu vezes aquela blanca quays sia corda.**
**E aprop tu met dejos aquela le ray entro que sia elevada e sia gitada de la codena, e sospen aquela am onci orp leon.**
**E aprop secsa autra seccio aprop aquela seccio per tres ditz, e aprop excorja la codena de la partida desus de la vena entro que apparia.**
**E aprop eleva aquela e inscideys aquela en deriera seccio deves le talo, e aprop extratz aquela e eleva aquela entro que sia yssida per la seccio segonda, e aprop extratz aquela de la seccio que es sobre aquela.**
**E fay aquo entro que extraguas aquela de la seccio que es pus sobirana o pus auta de totas las seccios, entro que tota es yssida; e lahoras inscideys aquela.**
**E si no obezeys a tu ad extrayre e elevar, lahoras intromet una agulha am fiel fort doble e ligua aquela e extratz la, o intromet dejos lu le ray e revolveys la tua ma a tota part entro quen sia getada.** **E guarda te que no sia inscidida; quar si es trencada, es fayt a tu dificil elevar aquela mot e es vengut sobre le malaute per aquella nouncement.**
**E cum aquela tota auras fora-gitada, lahoras pausa sobre le loc de la plagua lana submerssa en vi e oli rozat e oli no-rozat, e cura aquel entro que sia sant.**
**E si la vit es contrayta havent tortuositat a la qual sia envolucio a las partidas, e no es segon rectitut segon que havem dit, lahoras cove que tu fendas sobre aquela a tota partida de tortuositat de lu e als locs de envolucio de lu, e aprop suspen aquela am uncis entro que eleves aquella tota.**
**E guarda te deves la tua seccio que no inscidas la vena e que no plagues aquella, quar dificil sira a tu elevar aquela; e serva la tua prudencia en aquella.**
**Forma del inscident am le qual es seccada vit:**
**No es a lu accuitat ayssi cum als uncis ni es de aguda extremitat per so que no plague la vena; e es de grossa flexibilitat leon, quar si era subtil, inscidira la vena per la sua subtilitat; habantz es en lu superflua grosseza ayssi cum havem dit.**
**De extraccio venae cruris.**
**Aquesta vena es engendrada en las cambas en terras caudas ayssi cum al- Ategi en terra de Arabics e en las terras de India caudas e aridas de pauca teneritat e en las quals no nays erba ni aybre.**
**E fort leu es engendrada en altri locs del cors otra les cambas.**
**E la gestacio de lu es de putrefaccio que ve dejos la codena ayssi cum venen dedintz le cors serpentz e vermps e scarides e verms engendrantz entre la codena e la carn.**
**E senhal de la suscepcio de ladveniment de lu es de aquesta vena que accideys en la camba enflammacio vehement; e aprop le loc es vesicat; e aprop comensa la vena yssir del loc de aquela vesicacio quays sembla razit de planta.**
And then when the extremity appears, you should wrap around it a lead weight of one drachma and two drachmas, and wet it and leave the lead suspended from the bed.
**E tantas veguadas cum yeys de lu alcuna causa a las partidas defora, envolveys aquo em plom e noza aquel.** **E si mot es prolonguat, lahoras tu inscideys una partida de lu e envolopa le romanent; e no inscidas aquela de razit entro que sia fora yssida, quar si inscideys aquella es contrayta e intra en la carn e fa accidir apostema e poyredura en le loc e ulceracio mala.**
**Per que cove que sia tractada suaument e sia extrayta petit a petit, entro que sia fora-gitada del derier de lu e no remangua de lu alcuna causa en le cors.**
**E de aquesta vena es yssit en alcus homes que es en la sua longitut de v palms e de detz e ja es pervengut a mi que yssic un de xx palms.**
**E si es inscidida en la hora de la sua medicacio, lahoras intromet lo ray en le trauc de lu e perfora aquela am lonc trauc am le cors, entro que sia evacuat tot aquo that is in the materia, e administra putrefaccio del loc per alcus dias am medicinas; e aprop cura aquella per la curacio de apostemas.**
**E aquesta vena alcunas veguadas ha motz ramps, e majorment quan apar a la junctura del pe o en le pe, e veno a lu motz orrificis, e es yssit de quascu orrifici ram.**
**E donc cura aquela ayssi cum havem dit en la divisio e am aquo que es desus dit.**
**De sectione super vermes generatos sub cute et dicitur aegritudo bovina.**
**Aquesta malautia es nompnada en alcuna terra deves nos malautia bovina per so quar motas veguadas endeve als bious e es verm pauc un le qual es nat entre la codena e la carn, e va en tot le cos pujan e devalan, e es mostrat al sentiment deves le sieu anament de membre en membre entro que disromp la codena e yeys fora.**
**E la generacio de lu es per putrefaccio de alcunas humors ayssi cum accideysso verms e serpentz e lombrics e ascaridas en le ventre.**
**E es temut per la malicia de lu, quar cuando el va en le cors e es elevat al cap, e es pervengut al huel, lahoras fort leu uebre en lu e intra e destruyeys le huel, e aquo endeve motas veguadas.**
**E donc quandu voles curar aquel e extraire lu, lahoras no se fa si no deves la sieua ambulacio e apparacio de lu al sentiment, e adonc cove que tu strenhas aquo que es sobre lu e aquo que es dejos lu am liament e constriccio fort, e aprop secca sobre lu e extratz aquel.**
**E si es preondat en la carn e no le atrobes, lahoras tu pausa cauteri am foc sobre le loc entro que mora, e la major causa que es temuda es corrupcio de lu am la qual corrump le loc ayssi cum havem dit.**
**May si tu vezes aquel esser pervengut al cap prop del huel, lahoras strenh sobre le sobrecil am fort strictura, e aprop secsa sobre lu, e extratz aquel; e cove quel malaute use de mondificacio del sieu cors am medicinas evacuantz humors putridas malas, e guarda se de viandas generantz putrefaccio.**
**De sectione super aegritudinem nafir.**
**Aquesta malautia es nompnada en nostra terra nafir, e es dolor la qual ve en alcus membres, e aprop es permudada de membre en membre.**
**E yeu ja e vista aquela segon que yeu te recomtare.** **Yeu fu apelat a uma femna malauta ad una vila, e descubric le sieu bras e vi una imflacio petita en la vena funis del bras, e pus que fu romas per una hora, vi aquela imflacio anar ayssi cum va verm pujan ad aquest, mays pus leugierament que esser por, ayssi cum si fos argent viu quan corr de loc en loc.**
**E adonc anet sen la dolor de aquel loc e fiquet se en le muscle, e aprop aqu stec per una hora.**
**E aprop correc en lautre cors entro que pervenc al altre bra.**
**E aprop recomtec a mi que revolvia se per tot le cors sieu segon que yeu vi; e fo trop meravelat de la permutacio de lu e de la velocitat de membre en membre.** **E yeu ja havia vist denant aquo en les mieus huels segon aquella manieyra, empero yeu he vistz motz les quals atroban dolor esser permutada de membra a membre.** **Mays no vi aquo am les huels ayssi cum en la femna.**
**E yeu no cogiti esser aquo sino que es per aquo quar la femna era de viela, on so de secs cors e de venas descubertas, e en aquesta apparec al sentiment aquela ventositat permutada.**
**E es necessari que no apparesca segon aquesta retro-curacio en aquels que son delicioses e am cors humitz de venas ameguadas.**
**E cum tu voles la curacio de lu, e le pacient sent aquela dolor, lahoras no es a tu aparent al huel ayssi cum havem dit, lahoras tu strenh sobre aquel e dejos lu leugierament e secse sobre
**Mays si tu no la vezes am los tieus huels, alhoras tu cura aquel am excussio del cors e am aquo que expelleys ventositatz, e carmina aquellas am pillulas fetidas e am pillulas de serapi e semblantz.**
**De extraccio de sagetas.**
**Sagetas son diversificadas segon las specias, e segon les locs dels cors en les quals cazo, quar la lor diversitat es que de aquellas so que han grans puntas, e petitas, e concavas, e sordas, so es solidas; e de lor so que han tres angles, e de aquelas a las quals so que han lenguas; e de aquelas a las quals so astelas.**
**E dels senhals del servel es quan catz en lu sageta, e trespassa le os, e es yssit del cyphac le qual es sobre le cervel, quar accideys per lu soda vehement, e scotomia, e vertige, e rogor en les huels, e imflamacio e rogor de la lengua, e spasme e permixtio de entendament e vomi de colera, e fort leu es abscindida la paraula e es destruida la votz, e es yssit del loc de la plagua humiditat blanca semblant a pols, e yeys de lu semblant ad aquositat de la carn.**
**E donc si apareyso a tu aquestz senhals, lahoras tu abste de la curacio e de la extraccio de la sageta, si non es fora.**
**Mays les senhals de la sageta quando catz en le cor, so que ela es prop de la mamila senestra, e sent am aquela quays sia ficada en causa dura, e no es causa vueda; e fort leu le movement de la sageta es semblant a movement del pols, e corr de la plagua sanc negra, e siec aquel fregiditat de las extremitatz, e suzor freja, e sincopi; e donc sapias que la mort descen ses tot dopte.**
**E les senhals quan la sageta ha plaglat le pulmo so eyssiment de sanc spumos de la plagua, e les vayssels that so prop del col so apostematz, e es mudada la color del malaute, e expira sperit gran aut, e demanda atraccio de ayre freg.**
**E si catz la sageta en le velament le qual es en le pietz, e la dolor lahoras es prop de las costas petitas, e es fayt le ale gran am vehement dolor e am sospir, e no so maugutz totz les membres dels muscles.**
**E si catz la sageta en le stomac, lahoras fort leu yeys de la plagua vianda alcuna indigesta.**
**E si catz la sageta en le ventre, e es ficada en lu, yeys alcuna fenda de la plagua, o la tela, o budel le qual es disromput, e no es sperana en la curacio de lu extraccio de la sageta.**
**E si la sageta catz en la vesica, e es yssida defora urina, e procesesca de lu alcuna causa a las partidas defora, e fort leu es dolor sobre le malaute, lahoras sapias que es mortal.**
**Mays les autres membres ayssi cum es la cara, le col, el golayro, e las spallas e le adjutori, e les spondils del dos, e la furcula, e la coysa, e la camba e a lor semblantz dels membres, son salvatz segon las majors disposicions quando la sageta no atroba vena ni arteria e no es sageta venenosa.**
**E yeu recomtare aquo a tu que he vist del esser de aquestas sagetas, per que signifiques per aquo sobre la curacio tieua.**
**La qual causa es, quar en un home cazec sageta en le lacrimal del huel de lu en la razitz del nas, e yeu extrayssi aquela a lu del autra partida, dejos le grays de l'aurelha de lu, e es sanat, e no accidic en le huel de lu nocument.**
**E extrayssi autra sageta a un Juzeu la qual cazec en lu en lo grays del sieu huel, dejos la palpebra pus dejos, e la sageta ja era occultada e no so conseguit de aquela sino una petita extremitat am la qual adhereys al sieu fust, e era gran sageta de las sagetas agudas dels Turcs , am ferr leon en la qual no havia aurelhas.**
**E senat es le Juzieu , e no accidic en le sieu huel mal accident.**
**E extrayssi una autra sageta a un home Crestia la qual era cazuta en le golayro, e era sageta arabica, e es aquela a la qual so aurelhas; e adonc yeu inscidegui sobre aquela entre doas guidegi, e ja era submersa en le golayro de lu; e adonc yeu so subtiliat am aquela, e aprop extraxi aquela, e es sanat le Crestia .**
**E extraxi autra sageta a un home la qual era cazuta en le sieu ventre, e cogitegui que moris per aquella; e donc, pus que foro passatz xxx dias e no es mudat sobre lu alcuna causa de las suas disposicions, inscidegui sobre la sageta e engenagui sobre aquela, e es sanat, e no accidic a lu accident mal.**
**E vi mays un home en le qual cazec uma sageta en le dos de lu, e consolidada es la plagua sobre lu, e pus que foc aprop set ans, yssic la sageta en la razitz de la coyssa.**
**E vi una femna a la qual cazec sageta en le sieu ventre, e la plagua es consolidada dedintz lu, e no es mudada en las suas disposicions en re, e la femna no atrobec nocument en alcunes de les suas operacions naturals.**
**E vi un altre home al qual cazec sageta en la sua cara e consolidada es la plagua e romas la sageta, no atrobat aqui mota dolor, e motzsemblantz ad aquestz.**
**E extrayssi la sageta del home dels princeps del rey que era cazuda en le mieg loc del nas seu e ja havia declinat a la partida dreta un petit, e occultada era tota la sageta.**
**E yeu fu appelat a la curacio de lu aprop le cazement de la sageta entro a tres dias.**
**E adonc yeu atrobegui la plagua de la sageta mot streyta; e adonc yeu inquirigui aquela am tenta subtil, e no sentigui aquella; mays el la sentia puncio dejos la aurelha dreyta, e adonc speregui que aquella punccio era per la extremitat de la sageta.**
**E amplastregui le loc am emplaustre en le qual es vertut atrectiva e digestiva, confizant de mi quel loc se apostemes per que appares a mi le loc de la sageta, per que secces sobre aquela.**
**E no accidic en le loc accident significant que la sageta hagues conseguit aquel loc; e yeu continuegui am le emplaustre sobre lu per motz dias e no accidic accident; e consolidada es la plagua entretant, e romas le malaute de la extreccio de lu per spazi de motz dias entro que un jorn sentic la sageta dintz le sieu nas e recontec aquo a mi.**
**E adonc yeu pausegui sobre la plagua medicina acuta corrosiva per motz dias entro que foc ubert, e am la tenta yeu assagegui aquel, e atrobegui la extremitat de la sageta subtil, la qual adhereys al fust.**
**E aprop yeu ajustegui en la apersio de la plagua per aquela medicina acuta entro que aparec a mi visiblament la extremitat de la sageta, e passec a mi temps am aquo per le spazi de temps entro quatre months.**
**E aprop pus que la plagua foc amplificada, e foc a mi possible entrometre las forfexs en lu, e remaure aquela, e no obezic ad eyssiment, lahoras yeu no cessegui subtiliar e ingeniar sobre aquela am manieyras de engen, entro que comensegui un dia sobre aquela am manieyras de engens pendre lu am forceps decentment faytas, segon que vindra la forma de aquellas en la fi del capitol, entro que extraxi aquella; e aprop restauregui aquela plagua.**
**E alcus metges jutgavan que la cartillage del nas no es restaurada, e yeu restauregui aquela e la plagua es consolidada, e sant es le malaute per sanetat entiera, e no noguec en lu en deguna causa.**
**E yeu recomti a tu la qualitat de extraccio de alcunas sagetas per que pauses aquo regla e significacio sobre aquo que no he dit, quar las partidas de aquesta art e las definicions de aquela no so comprehendudas am narracio ni no comprehen aquelas el libre.**
**E le artifexs savi compara am pauc sobre mot; e am aquo que es present sobre aquo that es absent; e atroba operacio novela e instrument novel deves le descendement de las causas extranhas del art quan accideysso.**
**E donc yeu dic que sagetas no son fora-gitadas dels membres en les quals son ficadas sino segon dos manieyras: o per atraccio del loc en le qual intrec; o per le contrari de la autra partida.**
**E aquela que es gitada per le loc don es intrada, o es sageta procedent en loc carnos, e es atirada e fora-gitada.**
**E si no obezeys a eyssiment de la hora en la qual catz, lahoras cove que tu la laysses per alcus dias entro que poyresca la carn que es al enviro de lu, e sia alleujada l'atraccio de lu e la sua egressio.**
**E semblantment si es ficada en os e no obezeys a tu a eyssiment, lahoras layssa aquela per alcus dias e itera aquela am atraccio e mocio en quascun dia, e ja es fora-gitada.**
**E si no obezeys a tu eyssiment aprop alcus dias, lahoras cove que tu perforas en le circuit de la sageta en aquel os de tota partida am taravel subtil entro que'l loc sia amplificat de la sageta, e aprop extratz aquela.**
**Mays si la sageta ja es amaguada en le loc del cors, e es amaguada del sentiment, lahoras tu inquireys aquela am tenta, e si tu sentas aquela, lahoras atira aquela am alcus sturmentz les quals so convenientz a la atraccio de lu.**
**E si no podes sobre lu per la constriccio de la plagua e per la longitut del preon, e aqui no es os ni nervi ni vena, lahoras tu fen sobre la plagua entro que sia amplificada e que sia possible extrayre la sageta.**
**E si so a lu aurelhas am las quals sia tenguda, lahoras tu deliura la carn en la qual es ficada de tota partida am tot le engen that poyras far; e ingenia sobre aquo, si no podes sobre la evasio de la carn en la fractura de las aurelhas e en torssio de aquelas entro que obezesca.**
**E quan tu administras la extraccio de la sageta en quascun loc on sia, lahoras tu usa am torcio de la tua ma am forceps a totas partidas entro que fassa aquela obezir; e subtilia am deriera subtilitat que la sageta no sia trencada e que sia fayta a tu dificil atraccio de lu e de aquela extraccio.**
**E si no podes sobre aquela de la tua hora, lahoras tu layssa per alcus dias entro que se poyrescan les partidas que so en le circuit de lu, e aprop itera aquella quar lahoras es alleujada.** **Mays si a tu fa contrarietat flux de sanc, lahoras tu administra aquo que havem dit de curacio en le sieu capitol.**
**E guarda la tua vertut de inscizio de vena o de nervi, o de corda, e aministra engen en tota manieyra a tu possibla de la evasio de la sageta; e fay aquo am facilitat e tranquillitat e tarditat e fermetat ayssi cum yeu e a tu recomtat.**
**E donc que fassas contrayre la sageta per so quel malaute sia segon la figura segon la qual foc deves le cazement de la sageta en lu, quar es mays juvatiu.** **Mays si aquo no es a tu possible, lahoras tu aministra aquo que es a tu possible per les figures.**
**Mays las sagetas que son fora-gitadas per le contrari del autra partida, o que ja de lu procezeys alcuna partiade les partidas de fora, o fa gilbositat la extramitat de la sageta per sentiment de la partiade pus desus de la codena propdana e vezes aquela eminent; adonc tu secsa sobre aquela; e sia la seccio segon la quantitat en la qual prenguan las forceps; e aprop atira aquela, quar ela es fayta leugiera a eyssiment.**
**Mays si es retenguda en le os, lahoras tu tortz lama segon contrarietat entro que la sageta enprema en le os, e amplifique a si meteys, e aprop extratz aquela.**
**E sino, layssa aquela per alcus dias, e aprop itera aquela entro quen yesca.**
**E si le fust de la sageta es en aquela, lahoras tu impelleys aquela am lu.**
**Mays si le fust es cazut e voles aministrar inpulsio, lahoras tu intromet e aquela, si es sorda, sturment concau per so que intre la concavitat de lu en la coa de la sageta e aprop impelleys aquela am lu.**
**Mays si la sageta es concava, lahoras tu impulleys aquela am sturment fort intrant en aquella, quar la sageta es alleujada per aquella.**
**E si la sageta es entoxiguada, lahoras cove que tu concaves touta la carn en la qual es le vere, si es a tu possible aquo, e aprop cura aquela am aquo que si conveneys.**
**E si la sageta catz en le pietz, o en le ventre, o en la vesica, o en le costat, e es propinqua per so que tu tocas aquela am la tenta, e es a tu possible secsar sobre aquela, lahoras secsa sobre aquella e guarda te de inscizio de vena o de nervi, e extratz aquela, e aprop cos la plagua si indigeys, e cura aquela entro que sia sanada.**
**Forma de forceps am las quals so atiradas las sagetas:**
**Sian las extremitatz de lor cum a bec de ausel que son faytas cum serra quando prendon sobre la sageta per so que no la layssen.**
**E de aquellas son faytas motas specias, grans, paucas e migieras, segon la quantitat de la grandeza de la sageta e de la sieua pauqueza, e de la amplitud de la plagua, e de la constriccio de lu.**
**Ayssi cum ray per so que sia alleujat le intrament de lu en la sageta concava e es impellida am aquel.**
**De fleubotomia de las venas.**
**Las venas de fleubotomia de las quals corr costuma de fleubotomar so .xxx.,** **De las quals so en le cap .xvi.,** **So es doas venas pulsatils las quals so aprop las aurelhas, dic alhasisain; doas herbas that so en les dos templars apparentz; e doas venas that so en doas lacrimals de doas huels que son appeladas aspicientz; e la vena preparada en le mieg loc del front, e la vena que es en la extremitat del nas; e doas guidegi que so al col; e doas venas that so en la labia desus; e doas venas that so en la labia dejos; e  aquestas so las venas that so appeladas algelic ; e so doas venas that so dejos la lengua.** **Mays las venas que so fleubotomadas en les brasses so .v.;** **Quar de aquellas es una cephalica, e es deves le latz silvestre; e le poble appela la vena del cap, e sorda, e es vena migiera, e es composta de un ram de la basilica, e de autre ram de la cephalica; e nomna aquella le poble vena de tot le cors, e basilica es vena la qual es pausada en le latz domestic, e es nomnada citillar, e nompnan aquella les vulguars vena del ventre; e funis del bras, e es pausada sobre le focil, e es aquela en la qual es fleubotomat, e es aquela que appar sobre le poutz per apparicio manifesta; e salvatella, e es la vena que es entre lo dit auricular el pus petit dit, e so en lu dos ramps.**
**E en le pe e la camba so tres venas; la una de aquellas es que es dejos la curvatura del denolh del latz silvestre; e la segonda es sophena, el loc de lu es dejos la camba del latz domestic; e la vena sciatica, el loc de lu es dejos la camba del latz silvestre; e en la camba son autras venas semblantz ad aquelas.**
**Le juvament de las venas que so aprop las aurelhas es a cataris antics e emigranea e sahafati e ulceracios del cap malas antiquas.**
**E la qualitat de sagnar aquellas es segon que yeu recomti a tu: es que sia ras le cap del malaute, e sia freguat le cap del malaute en le occipiti en le loc de amdoas las venas am drap ample am bona fricacio; aprop strenha le malaute le sieu col am una benda entro que apparan las doas e les locs de lor so aprop las aurelles en dos locs depremegutz del cap; e quereys aquela am le tieu dit, e si tu sentes le pols de aquellas am le dit tieu, aqui senha am tenta.**
**Aprop tu pren la lancea cutellar, e es aquela que es inscident, e aprop tu intromet aquel dejos la vena en la codena entro quel fleubotomi vengua al os.** **E aprop eleva la tua ma am la vena e la codena a las partidas desus e inscideys la vena am inscizio inscident.** **E sia la longitut de la inscizio la quantitat de doi ditz ajustatz o entorn de aquo; e fay yssir del sanc atant quant voles.**
**E aprop strenh am pulvils e layssa aquela entro que sia sanada.**
**E ja e precedit en le comensament del libre la inscizio de aquellas e de lor la cauterizacio.**
**Mays de las doas venas arterias que so als templars le juvament de la fleubotomia es a emigranea antiqua e sode malvada e obtalmia assidua e cors de superfluitatz acutas effusas als huels.**
**E la qualitat de fleubotomar aquellas es segon que yeu recomti a tu: constrengua le malaute le sieu col mot entro que apparan las doas venas al sentiment per appericio manifesta e sia demonstrat le pols de lor dejos le tieu dit; e lahoras tu senha am tenta.**
**E aprop tu eleva la codena desobre la vena a las partidas desus am le tieu dit indic, e intromet le fleubotomi inscident dejos, e eleva la vena en sus; e inscidey aquela ayssi cum has fayt en las doas venas autras; e fay correr del sanc segon la quantitat de la tua necessitant.**
**E aprop deslia la coartacio del malaute, e pausa le tieu dit sobre la vena per una hora, e aprop pausa sobre aquella coto e pulvils e strenh aquella desus am fort constriccio, e layssa aquela entro que sia sanada.**
**E ja es precedida la rememoracio de lor, e de aquellas la inscizio, e la atraccio en le comensament del libre.**
**E donc le juvament de fleubotomia de la vena del front es aprop la fleubotomia de la cephalica a las malautias antiquas de la cara e a emigranea e rogor e ulceracios fetidas.**
**E la qualitat de la fleubotomia de lu es segon que yeu recomti a tu; so es quel malaute strenha le sieu col am una benda entro que apparesca la vena; e aprop pren le insturment le qual es nompnat fossori del qual aquesta es la forma de lu:**
**Pausa la puncta eminent la qual es al cap del fossori sobre aquella vena e percuteys sobre lu am penche o am autre causa en la manieyra de lu, e layssa lo sanc correr segon la quantitat la qual voles; e aprop deslia la perforacio del malaute e strenh aquela entro que sia sanada.**
**E alcunas veguadas es uberta am fleubotomi lat, empero no cove quel fleubotomi sia de acuta extremitat ayssi cum les autres fleubotomis, abantz sia de lada extremitat, e fleubotoma aquela segon le tranvers, quar le os es propda e fort leu trencaria en lu le fleubotomi quan es subtil.**
**Mays le juvament de las dues venas que so als lacrimals de doi huels per scabia del huels per rogor e sebol en les huels, e a las malautias de la cara.**
**E la qualitat de la fleubotomia es quel malaute strenha le col sieu am una benda, e aprop fleubotoma aquellas, e tu sias stant sobre le cap de lu.**
**E sia fayta la fleubotomia segon le transvers a longitut un pauc am fleubotomi pauc, quar en le loc no es carn; e si le fleubotomi es subtil, fort leu la extremitat de lu es trencada.**
**E aprop fay correr del sanc atant quant es a tu necessari, e pausa sobre aquellas coto, e strenh aquelas per una nueyt, e aprop deslia aquellas.**
**Mays le fleubotomi de la vena del nas es conferent a febre acuta e a soda vehement, e a las malautias de la cara e emigranea e rogor que accideys en la cara, e majorment quan es antiqua.**
**E la qualitat de la fleubotomia de lu es quel malaute strenha le sieu col e aprop te le sieu nas am la tua ma sinistra, e pren le fleubotomi subtil lonc e fica aquela en le mieg loc del cap del nas segon rectitut, quar la vena no appar al sentiment aqui, e quar le sanc comensa a fluir tantost.**
**Cove que tu ultimes la tua ma am le fleubotomi petit a petit e fassas correr del sanc segon la tua necessitat; e aprop lia aquela per una nuoyt, quar aquella es restaurada leugierment.**
**Mays le juvament de la fleubotomia de las doas guidegui a constriccio de ale e a comensament de lepra e a motas malautias e inpetige e malas ulceracios corrosivas ayssi cum herpotromeno.**
**E la qualitat de la fleubotomia de aquellas es que el malaute strenha dejos quascuna en le sieu col am liament; e estia le artifexs sobre le cap del malaute, e le malaute sia sezent sobre una sezela.**
**E aprop fleubotoma la vena al lonc am fleubotomi ample petit a petit; e aprop extratz de sanc segon temprada quantitat o segon aquo que vezes de necessitat que es ad aquo; e aprop fay semblant del autra vena.**
**E aprop deslia le liament e strenh las doas venas am strictura migiera per so quel malaute no sia prefocat, e laysa entro al mati quand la plagua es sanada.**
**E le juvament de la fleubotomia de las venas algerich, comfereys a petitas apostemas e pustulas de la boca e corrupcio de las gengivas e malas ulceracios e fissuras, e a malas ulceracios que so en le nas e en le circuit de lu.**
**E la qualitat de la fleubotomia de aquellas es que fases cezer le malaute denant tu, e strenh le col de lu am una benda, e aprop revolveys las labias de lu e reguarda a doas venas de las quals la una es de la dextra de la labia e la segonda de la senestra; e la demonstracio de quascuna es per la negror de quascuna de amdos, e aquo mays es quar en le circuit de aquellas so venas menudas negras; e adonc inscideys cascuna per inscizio inscident.**
**Mays si dubitacio es dejos tu, e no sabes qual es de aquellas, lahoras tu enten a inscisio de la major de aquellas, e de la pus manifesta de aquellas.**
**E fay le semblant de las doas venas that so en las labias desus.**
**Mays de doas venas that so dejos la lengua le juvament es aprop la fleubotomia de la cephalica a prefocacios that so en le guolayro, a la malautia de la uvula, e a malautias de la boca.**
**E la qualitat de fleubotomar aquellas es que segue le malaute entre las tuas mas denant le solel, e eleva la lengua de lu, e reguarda dejos la lengua, de la un latz de lu vena e del autre latz vena, e la color de quascuna es declinant a negror.**
**E adonc fleubotoma quascuna; e
**E las tuas venas that so fleubotomadas en le coyde so en las quals corr costuma en totz les homes, e la fleubotomia de lor es fayta segon dos manieyras, o pongen am le fleubotomi mirtilat o olivar a subtilitat declinant; o secsar am fleubotomi cutellar, e apelha si alnessil, e aquesta es la forma de lu:**
**Sia le latz de lu ayssi cum vezes, e conveneys a obrir las venas concavas plenas procedentz apparentz grossas, e ad aquellas que conteno sanc gros torbat.**
**E aquest fleubotomi es de menor latitut e de pus subtil extremitat, e conveneys a fleubotomia de venas subtils that conteno sanc subtil citri.**
**Mays le juvament de la fleubotomia de la vena basilica la qual es una de tres venas: quar extratz le sanc de las malautias that so dejos le guolayro el col, e de aquo que siec le pietz el ventre.**
**E conveneys al fleubotomador, quan fleubotomia aquela, that guarde be aquela e sia sobre-temor en aquela, quar dejos lu ha arteria, e si erra e ajusta en la punctura del fleubotomi, inscidira aquela arteria e accidira fluxs de sanc, per so que cove that no fleubotomes aquela am fleubotomi pungent, abantz sia sectant cum alnessil.**
**E si no appar la basilica per apparicio manifesta, lahoras cove that tu laysses aquela e que tu mudes a la autre, o que cerques alcun ram sieu; o que fleubotomes en loc de lu finis del bras, quar aquela es manifesta; e secsa aquela am fleubotomi alnessil ayssi cum havem dit.**
**Mays si tu voles la fleubotomia de lu meteyssa, lahoras cove denant la strictura del bras that toches le loc entro que conogues le loc dels pols, e aprop senha sobre lu am tencha; e aprop lia le bra
**E quan tu vezes, cum strenhes le liament, imflacio en le loc que has senhat am tencha, lahoras aquela inflacio es inflacio de la arteria, e donc squiva aquela.**
**E si vezes le sanc fluir en la fleubotomia ayssi cum aurina de enfant, el sanc es subtil rog, lahoras sapias que es del sanc de la arteria; e lahoras tu coyta e pausa le tieu dit sobre aquel per lonc spazi; e aprop osta le tieu dit, e si lo sanc es abscindit, quar motas veguadas es abscindit, lahoras tu strenh le bras e layssa aquel.**
**E guardes le malaute de la moccio de lu, e sia sobre-temor de lu e no maugua aquel per alcus dias entro que sia sanat.**
**Mays si le sanc no es abscindit, e vezes that thou art not present medicine ad hoc, lahoras tu inscideys the arteria, si appar to thee; quar the extremity of it is contracted, and is abscinded the blood; or that thou takest a handful of fistic, and feneth it, and taketh one third part thereof, and strenhest it upon the place of the vein with strictura descending am liament e am pulvils entro al autra dia.**
**E lahoras si le sanc es abscindit, bo es; e sino, lahoras cura aquel am aquo del qual es precedit a la rememoracio del loc de las polveras abscindentz flux de sanc.**
**E la abscizio del sanc de lu es dificil en motas disposicions per le loc petit de la plaga e la possibilitat del liament del brao.**
**Mays de la vena fusca la fleubotomia es juvament que extratz lo sanc de la partida subirana del cap e a la partida dejos del cors; per aquo quar es composta de ram de la basilica e de ram de cephalica, ayssi cum havem dit.**
**E cove al fleubotomant aquella que sia sobre-temor en la fleubotomia de lu, quar dejos aquela es un nervi; e adonc si ajusta en la punctura del fleubotomi e atroba le nervi, accidira a lu stupor, e es difficil la sanacio de lu, e fort leu no es sanat de tot, E aquest nervi motas veguadas apar al sentiment; e si es ocultat ad alcus homes e es subtil e no es monstrat, lahoras cove que tu pauses le fleubotomi am le qual tu fleubotomas am seccio de alnessil, e evita le nervi am la tua fortalesa.**
**E si la vena es entre dos nervis, lahoras tu fen la vena en la longitut.**
**Le juvament de la fleubotomia de la vena cephalica es que atratz le sanc del cap e comfereys a las malautias dels huels.**
**E cove en aquest propriament, si vols que la fleubotomes pungen am fleubotomi olivar o am fleubotomi mirti; quar es la pus salva de totas las venas, quar no es dejos lu arteria ni nervi.**
**Mays empero fort leu es apostemat en alcus homes, quan no es fleubotomat en la primieyra percussio, mays no notz en re aquel apostema.**
**Le primier de lu es del qual cove que sapias que fleubotomia no es aministrada sino en conservacio de sanetat e per sperana de lu e cautela de aveniment de malautias, e que sia fayta fleubotomia en la una de las venas que so en le coyde, so es: cephalica, fusca e basilica; e que sia fayta fleubotomia al comensament de primavera, sobre dejun en primavera e autunnne, e en invern aprop la comestio, quan apparo significacios de repleci.**
**E sia fayta fleubotomia e le tertz dia o al primier pus que del jorn siran passadas tres hours.**
**Mays fleubotomia que es aministrada, mays quan provoca convenienza e necesitat ad aquo, o de nuoyt o de dia, en tota hora e en tot temps.**
**E cove que efant no sia fleubotomat entro que aja xiiii ans, e femna que sia prenhs no sia fleubotomada sino del quart mes entro al sete, e les viels no sian fleubotomatz les quals ja han passatz lx ans.**
**E cum alcu vol esser fleubotomat per qualque manieyra sia, cove that mondifique les sieus budels denant la fleubotomia am clisteri leon, si en aquels ha mota fenda retenguda, per so que las venas no atiro las superfluitatz en la fleubotomia dels budels, que son puridas, e que no noguan als membres principals.**
**E no sian fleubotomatz les pascientz naua sacertiva e crapula, ni evasent de malautia ni de ebretat entro que aquo sia remaugut aquo de lor, ni malaute de ydropici, e mays que fleubotomia sia temuda aprop colica passio e aprop vomit, e aprop cos de ventre, e aprop multiplicacio de coyt e de trebal e de exercici de dejunis o de vigilias e de tota causa que dissolveys la vertut, o sia corpore28 o animal.**
**E aprop considera en subtiliacio de humos denant aquo si le sanc es gros, am viandas e beures, e am medicinas si aquo es a lu possible ad aquo.**
**E aprop intre en banh si alcuna causa no prohibit, o sia excersitat per alcun exercici per so quel sanc sia subtiliat.**
**E pausa la fleubotomia de lu en le pietz del dia, so es enviro la hora de tercia, ayssi cum havem dit.**
**E perforsa te quel pietz de aquel sia guardat en aquel dia de totz mals accidentz animals, ayssi cum es angustia, ira, temor, e de totz accidentz corporals, ayssi cum es trebal e pena superflua e coyt e semblantz a lor.**
**E a la sua sezelha fassa esser presentz las causas en le us de la qual corr costuma dels homes am aromaticitat e odorament e am bals e semblantz ad aquels segon la cantitat de possibilitat.**
**E segua le fleubotomador sobre un coyssi que sia pus aut quel coyssi de aquel que deu esser fleubotomat.**
**E aprop extragua le sieu bras, e fregue aquel am la sua ma le fleubotomador doas o tres veguadas; e aprop strenha le liament am correia e involva aque
**E sia la strictura temprada, quar la strictura quant no es engual, o la strictura es am superfluitat, lahoras prohibeys de fluxs del sanc; o es am mollificacio, e lahoras prohibeys le cors del sanc eyssament.**
**E aprop la strictura, cove that aquel que deu esser fleubotomat fregue las suas mas ensemps between lor entro that las venas sian infladas, e sian declaradas al sentiment.**
**E aprop le fleubotomador unte le sieu fleubotomi am un pauc de oli antic propriament; e aprop pausa le sieu di indic de la ma senestra sobre aquela vena, dejos le loc del qual vol la fleubotomia, per que la vena fuja un pauc, e la percussio sia sessada quar de las venas es la qual atrobas ayssi cum corda fugent deves la fleubotomia, e de aquelas es que es plena de ventositat e quan pauses le fleubotomi sobre aquela es contrayta deves le fleubotomi, e es desceubut le fleubotomador; e le fleubotomi no uobre la vena, e si uobre, aquella es streyta.**
**E donc, per aquo cove quel fleubotomador sia fermat e sia sollicit en totas aquestas causas.**
**E aprop depause le fleubotomi, mays si la vena es huberta en una veguada, lahoras bo es; e sino, tu itera aquo autra vaguada dejos aquel loc un pauc, o sobre lu am festinacio, si le loc no es apostemat.**
**Et si le loc es apostemat, o le malaute se spauresca, lahoras tu le layssa per un dia o per dos, e no strenha le liament, quar fort leu atirara apostema caut, ni no intre en banh.**
**E aprop itera la fleubotomia si la ama.**
**E si la apercio es petita e corr sanc subtilment, e temes que non yesca sanc la cantitat que voles, lahoras tu itera le fleubotomi en aquel trauc segon rectitut e ajusta en la appercio un pauc, e fay aquo am festinacio denant quel loc sia apostemat, quar le loc es apostemat en motz homes deves pauca apercio.**
**Mays si vezes aquel ja apostemat, lahoras no iteres sobre lu, quar no escusa a tu alcuna cause; e pausa sobre aquel alcuna parti **E es milhor en aquest loc que oli e que les altre olis.**
**E semblantment aministra fenda de oli en tota fleubotomia am la qual fleubotomes las venas deves la prohibicio de cors de sanc, e fan aquo tyriaca alfadoc e sagzenea quan es pausat de la una de aquellas sobre le loc, quar le sanc es subtiliat e es revolvut quan es gros.**
**E si en le loc de la fleubotomia es engendrat gran apostema, quar motas veguadas accideys, e majorment ad aquel que no es stat sangnat sino aquella veguada, o en la apercio de la vena pauca, e lahoras tu coyta, e pausa sobre le loc sponja infuza en aygua e sal, un pauc scalfada, e strenh aquella per una hora, quar es dissolvut.**
**E cove that fassa aquo aprop le yssiment del sanc de aquela vena am compliment de lu o de autra vena.**
**E si roman en le loc per alcus dias alcuna negror o viriditat, no notz aquo; e si voles, pausa sobre aquel alcuna causa de aloen e de mirra dissolvut, o alcuna cause de suc de mentastre o de calament o semblant de lu.**
**E motas veguadas accideysso apostemas eeminences deves fleubotomia de la basilica.**
**E donc pausa la tua ma sobre aquela, e si lahoras tu atrobas mollicia deves la tua compressio sobre aquela, lahoras aquela eminencia es malvada e mala; e adonc guarda te que pauses sobre aquela alcuna causa de aquo que havem dit, quar fort leu fluira de la arteria sanc.**
**E fay emplaustre am aquo en que es stipticitat, per que le loc sia endurat, e aprop cura aquel am l'autra curacio entro que sia sanit.**
**E cove que extraguas del sanc a tot hom segon la quantitat de la sua vertut e segon la color vencent sobrc le sanc segon que appar.**
**Quar si le sanc es negre, lahoras tu le layssa yssir entro que sia rog; e semblantment si tu le vezes gros, lahoras tu le layssa yssir entro que sia subtiliat; e semblantment si es agut, entro que sia ostada la acuitat de lu.**
**E cove ad aquel que es ple e fort e ha ncessitade extraccio de sanc en una veguada, que sia amplificada la fleubotomia de la vena e le fleubotomi sia lat.**
**E en aquel que es freul, sia fayt le contrari de aquel, e cove que extragua aquel en tropas veguadas, e que le trauc sia streyt.**
**E le milhor que es administrat en fleubotomia de vena es que sia la seccio transversa, non punctura.**
**E aquesta manieyra de fleubotomia es salva de flux de sanc e de inscizio de nervi, e es pus lausabla e pus salva que fleubotomia segon latitut e longitut.**
**E a la qual es acostumat sobrevenir sincopi deves la fleubotomia, e cove que tu cures aquel denant la fleubotomia am un petit de pa infus en vi de milgranas o de oximel simple scalfat; e extratz a l u del sanc en tres veguadas o quatre.**
**E si es enfregiditat de compleccio, lahoras prengua denant la fleubotomia pa infus en eyssarop de mirra o en eyssarop de mel aromatizat am specias ayssi cum am pebre, canela, gingiebre e semblantz, o en eyssarop aromatizat e mot odorant.**
**E si accideys sincopi deves la fleubotomia, e es causa de lu issiment de mot sanc, lahoras cove que prengua en beure aygua de carn e eyssarop mot odorant subtil; e use de aromaticitat am algualea, e sia linit le sieu pietz am aquela.**
**E usa de las autras causas that havem ditas en la divisio en le capitol de sincopi per evacuacio.**
**E qui vol eventar le sieu bras e dissolver le sieu sanc segonda veguada, cove a lu del qual la fleubotomia es per mota evacuacio, e la vertut de lu es freol, que evacue le sanc petit a petit, so es segon la quantitat de la vertut en les dias continuables.**
**Mays qui vol eventar le sieu bras, e gitar lo sieu sanc segonda vetz, e le sieu cors es fort, lahoras fassa aquo aprop vii hours or nine of the first flebotomie.**
**Mays qui vol atirar le sanc del cors sieu al contrari de la partida a la qual declina, cove that sia eventat in the second day or third.**
**Mays aquel cors en le qual es mot sanc ja scalfat e es acuit e fa accidir febre, cove that sia gitat de lu sanc in one occasion and a great quantity be shed and the warning be amplified until syncope occurs, more than you have preserved all the conditions of flebotomia; and that you pause your hand over the pulse of the blood to prevent death instead of syncope, for many occasions end badly when the phlebotomist is ignorant and neglectful.**
**E no cove when you want to release the arm and evacuate the blood second time, since already the orifice of the vein is closed and it is difficult to issue the blood, that you press upon it with vehemence and bend it slightly, for this is too bad.**
**Habantz le layssa entro que sia fleubotomat segondament; o remau aquo am la acuitat del fleubotomi that es coagulat del sanc in the orrifici of the vein; or pause sobre aquel de tyriaca alfarach, or of sagzenea, and compress it with compression light entro que el sanc sia fora yssit.**
**E si la vena es apostemada, lahoras layssa aquela e no la toques until the apostema is sedat.**
**E si necessitat te provoca a evacuar le sanc segondament, e no es excusacio, lahoras tu sagna quello sobre aquel loc or in autre bras in autre vena.**
**E la vena apelada funis del bras is phlebotomed in loc of the fusca or of the basilica, when not obstructed or hidden, for it is composed of those.**
**E la qualitat de la fleubotomia de lu es that the patient introduces his hand into cold water until the pulse becomes more visible and the vein appears manifestly.**
**E aprop sia strengut sobre aquel am liement am strictura magnifico; e aprop fleubotoma segond le transvers petit, non latitudinally nor according to the longitude.**
**E sia la apercio ampla e sia la tua fleubotomia with the which thou fleubotomas that one on the junction of the arm and small.**
**E si es prohibido el flux de sangre, lahoras tu itera la mano en agua fra y deja que la sangre corre en el agua hasta que consigues lo que necesitas.**
**Mays if you were in the days of summer, then you are excused from the iteration of the hand in cold water, and the month is paused the flow of blood in cold water in winter.**
**And the phlebotomy of this vein is more safe than all other veins, because it leaves you with no pulsating vein or nerve.**
**And the phlebotomy of the vein of the right arm is corresponding to the diseases of the liver.**
**And the quality of the phlebotomy at that time is that you strengthen your hand with intent or with your own hand, more than you have put it in cold water, until the vein is swollen and clearly demonstrated; and then you will cut across, and if you do not see anything there, you will not be satisfied with this.**
**And be careful not to finish your hand with the phlebotomy, because you leave it so that the nerves of the fingers are exposed and bare.**
**And then move your hand into cold water and let the blood flow freely in it, for if you do not move your hand into cold water, the blood will clot in the opening of the vein and be prohibited from flowing.**
**And since the blood is extracted according to the quantity of necessity, then you should pause over the vein with oil and salt, so that it is not consolidated abruptly; and similarly, you should do the same for all other veins.**
**But the judgment of the phlebotomy of that on the left arm is that it corresponds to the diseases of the gallbladder.**
**And do the same in the phlebotomy of this one, just as you have done in the other.**
**And the judgment of the phlebotomy is related to diseases that are located in the lower part of the body, just like those of the kidneys, and also to retention of menstruation, and to diseases of the throat, and ulcers of old sores and joints, and their similar maladies.**
**And the quality of the phlebotomy at that time is that the patient puts his foot in cold water and presses on it until the veins appear; then he places himself on the joint of the foot with a cord, and the location of the vein is marked by a dot on the said foot, and from there it branches out in the face of the foot like a bunch of ramps.**
**And therefore phlebotomize the most ample vein below the knee, at the spot where the aggregation of blood is greatest, for it is better and more suitable.**
**And if you phlebotomize that on the face of the foot, then you should beware of the nerves that are below it on the face of the foot, and pause your phlebotomy as if you were to incise it.**
**And be the phlebotomy vain.**
**But if the bleeding is prohibited; then you should put the foot of that one in cold water and let the blood flow freely into it until it is evacuated.**
**And if the phlebotomist erred in the first attempt, then you should go back to the phlebotomy and do it a little more, for the spot is sore; and don't worry about the malady, but rather beware of the nerves as we have said.**
**And similarly do the same for the saphenous vein of the other foot as well.**
**And for the sciatic vein, the spot as we have said is below the tail of the partition of the wild forest.**
**And the judgment of the phlebotomy at that time is to be careful not to let blood flow when it is cautious.**
**And the quality of the phlebotomy at that time is that the patient should enter a bath, and hasten and strengthen the vein of that one from the lat to the width of the ankle up to the four fingers in a subtle band, so that it appears only through that.**
**And therefore, when it appears, then you should phlebotomize that one according to each individual's nature that is possible for you and according to the traverse, and it is better; or incise that one by incision or secede that one by section, because the spot of that one is sore.**
**And it is in the midst of men like a woman; and if you find that one, and it does not appear to your sense, then you should phlebotomize some branch of that one, and it is that which appears on the two sides of the foot below the said auricular and anular.**
**And beware of the nerves, and let blood flow in the quantity that you desire.**
**And approach the structure and pause over the spot of the phlebotomy cut and strengthen the spot, so that slightly it is healed.**
**Of the advantages and qualities of using those things.**
**Ventozations are of combs, or of horns, or of veerings.**
**And ventozation is done in two ways: one of them is by scarification and blood extraction, and the other is by ventozation without scarification.**
**And this ventozation that is without scarification is done in two ways, because one is with fire and the other is without fire.**
**And the 14 locations of the body where bloodletting with scarification and blood extraction is administered are: one in the area where pauses are made, which is the occipital bone at the back of the head; and the middle location between the two parts of the neck; and bloodletting below the mandible just below the mouth; and bloodletting on both sides of the mento; and bloodletting on the alohoster, which is located above the coccyx; and bloodletting at the end of the coccyx; and bloodletting at two points, each of which is located between two arm bones; and bloodletting on both sides of the pelvis; and bloodletting on both sides of the hipbones.**
**And bloodletting does not extract blood from the large veins, but rather from the small, scattered veins in the flesh, and therefore it is not a method for purging the body through those means, as it is done by phlebotomy; nor is it necessary to perform bloodletting with fire or without fire in any disease caused by repletion, until the entire body is evacuated.**
**However, if necessity arises due to illness or continuity, we shall administer the bloodletting at the beginning of the month and at the end of it, and in the middle of it, and at some other time.**
**And therefore when the moon is in its third or middle phase, we order bloodletting to be done more than two or three hours after sunrise.**
**And the judgment of bloodletting from the neck is that when it causes gravity in the head and down to the eyes; however, it is necessary that this be done after a thorough evacuation of the entire body.**
**And this bloodletting is in the location of phlebotomy of the cephalic vein.**
**And it is not permitted to use it on one who has a complete blockage or in whom there is catarrh, because it would give rise to great harm.**
**And therefore it is not necessary to use that on the elderly, and in those whose heads are afflicted with serious diseases.**
**But if one is continuing on that and it is done over there, forgetfulness ensues; and therefore you must command the bloodletting attendant to pause for a moment before opening the next vein, lest forgetfulness occur.**
**But bloodletting from the alkehel is in the location of phlebotomy of the vena fusca and basilica: and therefore it gives rise to asthma, constriction of the lung, scissura of the larynx, cough, and repletion.**
**And it is necessary that the bloodletting from the alkehel be done in a small amount, for if it is paused afterwards, it will engender weakness in the chest and stomach.**
**And the bloodletting from alhagdahan gives rise to accidental pains in the head and obtalmia, emigration, precocity, and pains in the roots of the teeth; and it is in the location of phlebotomy of the basilica.**
**And it is necessary that you command the bloodletting attendant to not press his hand with scarification, so that he does not cut into the artery and cause a flow of blood.**
**And bloodletting after the tongue gives rise to ulcers in the mouth, corruption of the gingiva, and similar afflictions as those that are in the mouth; and it is in the location of phlebotomy of the aliheric vein which is in the two lips.**
**But the bloodletting that is done on both spatulas gives rise to caphatan, which is caused by an excess of warmth.**
**And the bloodletting from both parts of the dentals gives rise to a judgment about the phlebotomy of three veins, namely the basilica, fusca and cephalica, because that attracts the blood from all those smaller veins that are in the flesh, and those smaller veins from other larger veins until it reaches an attraction to the three veins.**
**And command the bloodletting attendant not to proceed too quickly with scarification, for the location is stripped of flesh and leaves only nerves and arteries.**
**And it is a bloodletting in which one is bled over the ashoses and gives rise to hemorrhoids of the anus and ulcers below.**
**And it is necessary that you command the bloodletting attendant to be a great bloodletting, and of eram, because the location demands strong section; and strong, subtle bloodlettings are torn, and be scarified with scarification.**
**But small bloodlettings from the knees, manifestly so, because they attract the blood of all the body, and give rise to old pains in the lungs and the belly, and the bladder; and provoke menstruation, and give rise to bothor and demil; and are located in the location of phlebotomy of two saphenas, and alahorcoben, and two cavilhas.**
**However, they can damage the entire body and cause syncopal episodes in many men.**
**And the judgment of the alahorcoben bloodletting is similar to the judgment on the bloodlettings of two knees.**
**And the quality of the position of the bloodlettings is that one pauses the bleeding at the beginning, and sucks it up slowly with a gentle suction, and does not prolong the position of the bloodlettings, but rather pauses them slightly, and holds them quietly, and allows the humors to come forth naturally.** **And do not cease iterating until you see the location already reddened and inflated, and that the rigor of the blood appears.**
**And when you are ready, scarify and iterate the suction gradually, and carefully consider the disposition of the body.**
**Because that man who has tender skin and few pores, you must scarify him only once and not again, so that the location is not ulcerated.**
**And command the bloodletting attendant to amplify the scarification and proceed a little, and then apply suction with ease.**
**And if the blood is thickened, then it is necessary to scarify twice, because in the first scarification, the way of subtlety to the blood and its satiation is opened.** **But in the second scarification, one must carefully scrutinize the extraction of the thick blood.**
**And if the blood is very foul, then it is necessary to make a third scarification in order to achieve the desired result.**
**And finally, when we want to extract the blood gradually or in small quantities, it is enough for us to make one scarification.**
**And if we want to extract a lot of blood, we will scarify with many scarifications; and if we know that the blood is thick, then it is necessary to scarify slowly and carefully.**
**And the term of scarification in which is the depth of the incision as much only.**
**And if the incision is large, hard, and red, and its pores are very tight, it is necessary to lubricate the locations of the bloodletting with a gentle, open, and resolving oil; if it is in the summer, then use olive oil, or violet oil, or almond oil, or chamomile oil; and if it is in the winter, then use birch oil, or lily oil, or camomile oil, or blood oil, and to those similar.**
**And if the superfluity is great, fresh, then the oil should be amaranth, or balm of Gilead, or olive oil, or aniseed oil, and to those similar.**
**But if the bloodletting attendant has large pores of tender skin, then it is necessary that he be prohibited from using oil, and it is necessary that he apply water or fresh water from a source such as saltwater, cow's milk, or borehole water to the locations of bloodletting, and similar waters to those.**
**And that person whose blood is very wet, washes his bloodletting tools with vinegar or water of myrtle and sumac, and similar waters to those.**
**And that person whose superfluities are great, washes his bloodletting tools with old vinegar, or water of Sancho, which is majorana, or decoction of anise, or chamomile, and similar waters to those.**
**And it is necessary to keep the bloodletting before dinner; having to be administered about one hour or two hours before dinner, and it is necessary that he sleeps near the bloodletting.**
**What is the need that one must regulate the bloodletting before bleeding?**
**And consider at the beginning: then if the bloodletting attendant or he who must bleed is choleric and prone to inflammation of the blood, then it is necessary that he takes cooling causes, such as mugwort, bitter orange peel, endive with vinegar, lettuce, and scallion, and similar remedies.**
**And pause from their foods, such as potage, and fowl flesh, and prepared dishes with spices, and similar remedies.**
**And that person whose complexion is fresh, should take in drinking essence of almond or essence of alkanet seeds, and sumac, and wine with a mild scent between Easter and Christmas; and it is recommended that he uses moderation in drinking and eating, and pause from foods like potage, cabbage, and small birds and pigeons.**
**And it is necessary that on the day of bloodletting and bleeding, drink should be greater than food.**
**And it is necessary that he be given to drink in some hours before certain men tyriaca alpharac, or medicinal herbs of musc, so that the musketa is made, or alcelita before bloodletting or near it, so that the main members are comforted and the blood is subtilized; and it is not necessary for them to take those scalded.**
**But the bloodletting that is called scarification is bloodletting that is paused on the liver, and on the gallbladder and podagra, and on the umbilicus, in the locations of the joints, and the plexus of the spine, because these members do not tolerate scarification upon themselves.**
**And it is not sought after by those who have blood flow disease of the nose, but rather atraction of blood from member, such as pausing bleeding on mammary gland in the illness of bloody flux of the nose; and we use that to dissolve fresh viscosity of member, such as pausing on the abdomen and umbilicus; because that rarefies the member and cools it and relieves pain which is resolved by dissolving.**
**And it is paused over the tonsils when they are obstructed or swollen, because by virtue of strong attraction it opens up obstruction and eradicates swelling from its place.**
**And similarly, it does when paused over the liver and gallbladder to dissolve venosity in those who are enclosed.**
**And these bloodlettings are administered with suction only, and sometimes with heat.**
**And sometimes they are administered full of hot water in cases of gallbladder disease.**
**And this is why the bloodletting is filled and made greater, whether it is with cold water alone or water in which certain herbs are steeped to suitable proportions.**
**Form of bloodletting administered with heat: the width of the orifice should be two fingers, as we have formed it; and the quantity of the point should be half a palm; and it should be in the lat part of the instrument, in the place where it is in the circuit, one quarter of the instrument, the hole should be small according to the amount that an awl can enter into it.**
**It should be made of earthenware or citrine, with thick borders, lion, equal and third parts, in order that it may not disturb the member's position on it.**
**And it should be in the middle of a transverse beam made of earth or iron, where a candle is placed with fire.**
**And it is this bloodletting that is greater than the one we have recommended, and the small amount of blood that flows from it according to the diseases and state of the person who uses it.**
**And the bloodlettings of the elderly and exhausted are different from those of the young and robust.**
**And the quality of pausing this bloodletting with fire on the member is that it extends the ember with firewood decently in front of a small candle of wax, and pauses it over the middle of the transverse beam in the middle location of the bloodletting, so that the fire be kindled around the part left over so that it may not burn the patient's body.**
**And it is placed over the member of the patient, and the said thing is on the hole that we have mentioned, until when we have bloodletting and do not need to open the hole and let the vapor rise over that hole, then the bloodletting will be dissolved.**
**And blow gently with the ember according to its manner, and repeat that if you need it.**
**But in bloodletting that is administered in the disease of pleurisy, with water, where there is no transverse beam or hole, and it is not administered except when it is filled with water, and it is placed over the member only.**
**And this is the form of it: And as this bloodletting grows greater, so too does its quality, for it can receive a large quantity of water.**
**Chapter XCIX**
**Bloodlettings are not administered on fleshy members, but only on those where it is not possible to apply bloodletting cups, due to the small size of the vessels, similar to the blood vessels of the mouth and gums; or in a denuded member without flesh, similar to the nose and its surroundings.**
**And the quality of using those that you have found bloodletting cups which are in the waters of digestion and purgation.**
**And it is left the day and night in water until they are famished, and no cause remains in the belly of those; and it is evacuated the body by phlebotomy and bloodletting; and the member of the patient is thoroughly washed until it becomes red; and it is placed on it.**
**And when they are filled and stopped.**
**And if it is possible to suck out the place with bloodletting, it is more direct in judgment.**
**And if not, then wash the place with vinegar and water, and be squeezed and expressed.**
**And if the blood is prolonged in the body near the closure of the bloodletting cups, and this liquid begins to run out, then put a cloth soaked in cold water on it, and keep it there until the bleeding stops.**
**And if the blood is multiplied, then sprinkle vitriol powder or powdered gallnuts and similar substances of stiptic causes over it, until the blood is absorbed; or place the warm poultices on the location and leave them until they adhere to the location, and the blood is absorbed.**
**And thus, if necessary, iteration of bloodletting cups, when it is possible to change those.**
**And if the bloodletting cups are prohibited from suspension, then wash the location with recent blood or leave an acupuncturist's needle in the area until there is bleeding; and be careful, because those that feel some blood will soon absorb it.**
**And when you want to stop them, sprinkle a little bit of powdered aloes, or salt, or ashes, and then cauterize.**
**Thus begins the third part: of restoration.** **This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine; and it is the restoration of fractures and accidental dislocations in the bones.**
**Oh, foolish son, understand that those who boast about this chapter are the ignorant doctors and common people, and those who have not read the books of the Ancients nor glanced at a letter from them.**
**And because of this reason, it is made that this method of the sages in our land is private; and you must not forget it at any time, nor attribute anything to chance, but only through the prolonged reading of the books of the Ancients and study on their understanding, until I extract the science from them.**
**And thus, I have directed my efforts towards experiment and study in the length of my own life.**
**And you have already been described in this chapter all that contains my science and on which my experiment has passed; therefore, I have briefly presented it to you others and released it from the occupation of elongation; and have summarized it at the end of summarization; and have shown it at the end of declaration; and have formed it into many forms of instruments that are administered in this way, as is done by addition of declaration, just as I did in two previous chapters.**
**Chapter One.**
**Summary and collections from fractured bones, for which a previous necessity is required before we begin to remember the members of fractures and their various forms.** **Therefore, let us say in the preamble to this chapter the summaries of the sermon; and let us consider the headings under which the artists are forced to stand at attention regarding the truth of these matters; so it is you and those who are eager to know or learn this noble art, other than yourselves.**
**And thus I say that when you encounter any fracture or dislocation or twisting or separation, then it is necessary for you to turn back to the beginning with phlebotomy or to alleviate that, or whatever else together, if no obstacle prevents it, just as debility of virtue, or the one who suffers it, or old age, or time of intense heat, or of intense cold.**
**And thus it is content in its own food of fresh herbs and fowl meat and crabs; and prohibit gross meats and fill them with viands and all manner of food that fills the veins of blood, until you are secure from apostema and if not fear effusion of matter to the member.**
**And then return the patient to their original regimen with which they are accustomed to.**
**And therefore, when the broken bone begins to be restored, it is necessary that the patient be fed with nutritious foods of great and strong and heavy consistency, in which there is viscosity, such as foods made from wheat cooked with water, rice, and similar substances, and also meat, fish, and eggs, and thick soups, and milk of cows, and juices of fresh fruits, and all sorts of food that are similar to these, and under this regimen, the coagulation of the fracture is done more easily and gently.**
**And you should know that the bones are brittle when they are in old men who are in their first old age and in those who are decrepit, it is not possible for them to be continued and consolidated according to their nature by the desiccation of the members of theirs.**
**But nature adjusts and connects the broken bone of all parts without any similar cause, like glue that thickens and adheres to it, until it is conjoined and joined together, until the end of fortitude and firmness, just as fire at the beginning, until no cause prevents that from its works.**
**And for this reason it is necessary that you pause the foods of the patient, foods in which are gravity and viscosity and thickness, just as we have said.**
**And you should know that the species of fractures are diverse according to the diversity of the members, for a fracture of the femur is different from a fracture of the skull; and a fracture of the foot is different from a fracture of the arm; and similarly all the other members are different between them.**
**And you should remember all the species of fracture, exposed in its own chapter distinct from others.**
**Many different kinds of fracture in itself.** **And the species of fracture are diversified in their own kinds; for there is a curved fracture and another that occurs in the stars; and some times it is made according to the length of the bone: and these are fractures of the satagia and astelhas and additio
**And every species has its own unique pain or torment in the process of restoration, according to the distinct memory of each place.**
**Many signs of bone fracture.** **And for this reason it is known that there is a fracture of the bone: it is the twisting of the bone, and the prominence or swelling of the bone to the sense, and when you compress the bone with your hand.**
**And therefore, when there is no apparent twisting or prominence and you do not feel a sense of resistance when you touch the bone with agitation, nor does the patient experience great pain, then there is no fracture here.**
**It is possible that there may be twisting or small fissure, therefore it does not matter if you compress the bone with your hand and all its surroundings; but rather pause over it, taking into account the medicines of which there is memory in this moment, which corresponds to this place; and so be strict by subtle subtlety.**
**And you should know that the place when it is curved and not split in two or another way that does not occur in the satagia, as all parts of its comparison are remade, then it is necessary to begin from your hour to correct it, having taken into account what will happen apostema caution.**
**And if apostema caution occurs at that place, then let it be left for several days until the apostema ceases; and then equalize it according to each manner that you can with lightness and ingenuity.**
**And you should know that the restoration and equalization of the bone is easier than in the case where satagia occurs.**
**And so strengthen that according to what will come in the memory of it.**
**However, if in the bone there are satagias, then it is necessary to extend this broken member of two parts, whether it be the arm or leg; or with your hand if the member is small; or with two ropes or one rope and hand.**
**And be in the position with which you pause the member in its natural figure, while the parts are extended from the broken member, then you will be forced to return those additions with ingenuity and according to each manner that you can in their places.**
**And take care to follow your strength, so that what you do does not harm the patient through your operation or injury; and strive according to your power to apply one bone to another, their companion in better forms.**
**And it is necessary that at that hour you act with profit and touch that place with your hand, and if there is some other cause here, correct that and equalize that according to the quantity of your virtue.**
**And excessive extension and compression, just as foolish doctors often do, which cause apostema caution to occur through their operation, or cause contraction in the member, just as we have seen before through the operation of theirs.**
**And the quality of the strictura of the member at rest is that which you recommend; because you know that broken members are diversified in their smallness and greatness and in the form of those.**
**And of those that are small, like the arm and leg and foot, it is necessary that the wrapping be made of very fine cloth.**
**But those that are large, like the thigh or leg, it is necessary that they be wrapped in a thick and strong cloth, because the gentle wrapping connects the large member and strengthens it from all parts with a strict equalization, so that nothing enters into it.**
**And thus, begin, and with your evacuation of equacio, pause momentarily convenient to that place, over the location of that fracture with three or four wraps as the member requires; and strengthen your hand a little with the wrapping.**
**And thus, come to that part of the location of the fracture which is most superior, and strengthen more than not so as to keep your strictura with which you have strengthened the location of the fracture.** **And thus, stretch yourself to the wrapping of the location of the fracture a little, and gradually loosen the strictura bit by bit, until you take from it a great part.**
**And thus, take another bandage and wrap it around that other spot on the broken location with wrapping, and thus come to the wraps at the most distant part of the fracture; and be your operation in the strictura of the wrapping and in mollification of that according to what we have said in the first wrapping above.**
**And thus, pause between the wrappings of stopa leon or cloth with which the twisting of the fracture is equalized, if there is twisting in it; and if not, you do not pause.**
**And thus, pause over another bandage, and thus equalize over these wrapping stars made decently soon, if in the location there is no inflammation or cautionary apostema, and then pause over that which seats the apostema and prevents the inflation; and leave it for a few days; and then you strengthen over those stars.**
**And the stars of the wrapping are made of the middle part of canna lada reed, and well formed; or they are made of ash wood; or of palm tree branches; and the width of each star is according to this form and figure:**
**However, it is necessary that the star which is paused over that fracture be a bit larger and thicker than the other stars, and the length of the star according to what is measured by the member in magnitude and smallness; and thus strengthen over the stars with another bandage according to your first strictura; and thus bind above with a cord decently according to what we have said about strictura, and it should be your strictura according to the location of the fracture more, and as much as is lengthened from the fracture, so much less the strictura.**
**And it is necessary that the threads be of a moderate thickness and subtlety, and be made of silk; and if the threads are thick, just as I have seen in the operation of certain foolish people who pause their threads with cords of twisted silk, and it is a great error, when the strictura is not in equalization.**
**And it is not necessary to use very fine threads, because you will not consecrate with them according to the strictura that you want, and it does not matter if between star and star there are less than a digit.**
**And if the patient is led by the extremities of the stars to the strictura in its own locations, then pause with those of stopa leon or woolly camel hair until it does not cause harm.**
**In some cases, the fracture is accompanied by a plague, and accidents of disruption occur in the code, and you will come with remembrance in that one in the capital according to singularity.**
**And you should know that not every broken member is strengthened with stars on the first day; the reason being that the member, when it is large, does not need to be paused over by stars immediately, but rather after a few days or seven or more, according to your safety precautions for cautionary apostema.**
**And this is the method of the ointments with which the Ancients restored, which are paused over fractures and dislocations and torsions.**
**Method of ointment like a refreshing balm for the restoration of fracture, suitable for many complexities and most particularly for women and children, since it is applied to that which does not feel heat or cold: and it is that you take from powder of millstone, and it is the marrow of the flour that falls off the movement of the millstone in the walls of the mill.**
**And thus it is comfortable as it is, unless you sift through it with an album of honey, and pause the thickening or thinning; and then use it.**
Another method for applying an ointment to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: recipe of assafetida, lapdanum, acacia, enula, and myrrh, which is the essence of sage, one drachma ten; of myrrh and aloes, one drachma five; of alochil, one drachma twenty; all are mixed with water or album of hog's gall if the patient's complexion is scorched; and then use this ointment, which has a good composition and restores broken bones slightly, and gives strength to old men.
Another method for applying an ointment that restores fractures and twists: recipe of myrrh and white altai, one drachma ten; of myrrh and aloe, one drachma five; of acacia, one drachma six; of Armenian balsam, one drachma twenty.
**All are to be pounded in a mortar with a wooden pestle, and sifted, and mixed with water or honey, and administered.**
**Method of ointment for joints and bones separated from their places, and sudden pain occurring in those and fissures and fractures: take fine wool and immerse it in sweet wine and olive oil and pause over the location.**
**But in this ointment there is no virtue of restoration, of cautionary apostema and propelling out pains properly.**
**Another method of ointment that restores broken bones: take leaves of fig tree and leaves of wild poppy; mix all together and make an ointment from them.**
**Short method of ointment to be administered for the restoration of fracture of bone and when you desire resolution of the remnant of apostema: recipe razed from alta, camomile, flowers of violets, flour of ears, all mixed together.** **And all are to be pounded and mixed with wine, if the member is not scarred.**
**But if it is scarred, labor and comfort that one with water of colandro moist or with water and use of lead.**
**Another method of ointment more powerful in resolution than the first, when apostema persists and hinders the restoration of the member: recipe razed from alta and seed of lily, and balm, melilot, majoram, flowers of violet, camomile, all mixed together.**
**But Hippocrates does not advise freely that it should be applied to the member torn apart for its restoration, but rather a composition of wax and oil is made and no other cause; and recommends that it should be mixed between grossness and subtlety.**
**But at Gualia it is seen that it should be applied to the member torn apart for its restoration and the causes in which there is dryness with a small degree of heat like myrrh, onions, and similar substances are used just as those causes which have been recommended.**
**Method of ointment that comforts lesions and pain: recipe mixed with cypress, human hair shaved or bird's feather, and alta, and salt, all mixed together; pound and sifted and mixed, and made into an ointment.**
**But the quantity according to which it should be left to remain in the wound and how it should be divided is that you consider whether there is not pain or pruritus or if the bone is broken and not in its place, then you do not want to leave it for many days.** **And if it happens that a violent pain or pruritus or inflammation occurs at the site, then you should withdraw or remove that in the hour, and stop the application of the ointment.**
**And take linen cloth and marine sponge lioness wet, and immerse that in boiling water, and with that wash the location until the pruritus ceases and the pain is calmed; and then let the member rest for an hour; and then pause over it with fine wool soaked in sweet wine and oil or red oil, and lie on it for a night until you are sure of caution from apostema, and that inflammation of the member subsides, and the pain of it is eased.**
**And then gently iterate that subtle stricture and small ointment, and do not strain it with your first constriction, and subtlety apply it until it is healed.**
**And if at times the apostema and the rigor and the pain and the inflammation and all the accidents are completely gone, and you need ointment and stricture, then you should iterate that in the same way as you did at the beginning equally.**
**And if there is no cause in the member that we have said, then you should not leave it until at least three or four or five or seven days.** **and some times everything is left for 20 days according to how it appears to you by the relaxation of the member, just as we have said, until the fracture adheres and approaches the coagulation of the flesh on that.**
**And then adjust in the stricture more than your first constriction all, and adjust in the thickening of the flesh of the patient, according to how it is preceded by the remembrance of that.**
**But if you find the location of the fracture already dry and exhausted more than it should be, then you know that the nourishment is prohibited from reaching that; and therefore, take up that with boiling water every time you remove that; and do this for all three days; and relax the stricture a little, and by this operation, the nourishment reaches the member, and is healed gradually.**
**But this is what foolish restorers of the fracture of the member do another way when it is not restored at first, according to what is right, and is restored in a tortuous manner, it is an error according to their operation, and great fear, and if they had written this out fully, the Ancients would have added more to this.**
**And I have not seen anyone of them do this, therefore it is more reasonable that this does not happen.**
**Chapter 2: Of fracture when it occurs in the head.**
**The species of fractures are many, and the figures of them are diverse, and the causes are distinct, because some fractures are caused by percussion of space, and the percussion breaks all the bone into small pieces, leaving it like a stick, and therefore this species is called asciatical; or the space insinuates itself into some part of the bone, and insinuates itself into the flesh and does not pass through to the other side; and this species of fracture is called levatio absoluta.**
**And the wound of these two fractures is either great or small, and of fracture that is concave or convex; and cause of it is percussion with a hammer or falling on the forehead, and to their likenesses.**
**And this fracture is either penetrating, which approaches the panniculus (fatty tissue) that is left behind the bone; or it is on the surface of the bone, and the wound of these two fractures is either great or small.**
