**And the fracture is one that is split in the bone, in the subtlety of hair small, and therefore it is named this species fracture capillary.**
**And it is a fracture that is caused by falling or percussion of the forehead and similar, which causes some bone plate to enter into the inward parts, and is done in the concavity as if it were happening to the skulls of the ancient ones when they were hit by percussion and their entrance was broken into the inward parts.**
**And most of the time it is done in the skulls of human beings, just as if they were made by children.**
**And all these types of fractures that are scattered, are as bad as stars separated.** **And you will remember everything about this in its place.**
**And you will know all these species of fracture by detection over those and by inquiry into their causes and showing the corrupted flesh that is on them.**
**And the species of fracture capillar is known by this that it is discovered on the bone, and it is wiped away, and it is lined over there with a tent, because the fracture appears black.**
**But in the treatment of fracture, consider first the accidents of the patient, and then if you find that they are accompanied by manifest signs of fear, such as vomiting of bile, extension, loss of understanding, absence of speech, syncope, acute fever, and swelling of the eyes and rigor of those, and similar manifestations to theirs in greater dispositions, unless the doctor is not cured.**
**And if there are non-corresponding accidents, you hope for salvation, then you begin the treatment of him.**
**The cause is that if it has come to you like a plague in the beginning as it is plagued and this is on the days of winter, then it is necessary that you study in the examination of the bone before the 14th day according to all disposition.**
**And if it is in the days of summer, then it is necessary that you cover the bone before the 7th day, having that which is left on the bone be corrupted by the panniculus, and that accidents occur as we have recommended.**
**And if the fracture has already penetrated to the panniculus and covered the brain, and is in small parts and concavity, then it is necessary that you inscribe the comminuted and attrited part, according to what I have recommended to you.**
**And that you reason with the patient's head plagued, and discover on the bone according to custom and manner to your possibility, and that it be lighter on the patient.**
**And if it happens to you that the detection of the bone is required, or there is a flow of blood or an abscess that is warm, then you should oppose yourself to it in accordance with what is necessary, and do as follows: fill the wound with infusions of vinegar and rose oil, and make the wound rest until the abscess is sedated, and ensure that the flow of blood is stopped; and begin with the excision of the bone and the removal of the affected area.**
**And it should be done according to one of two ways of operation.**
**And the one way is that you inscribe the bone with an inscription of straight line, and this is the form of it: And then administer another inscription to this, a little more late than that; and this is the form of it:**
**And then administer the inscription, but later than the second.**
**And it is necessary that you have different inscriptions, some of which are longer than others; and some of theirs are shorter than the others and are in the later stage of their extremities, and are made of iron or lead.**
**And use them according to their facility in percussion on the inscription, so that it does not concuss the head and lead it astray.**
**And if the bone is strong and hard, then it is necessary that you perforate in the circle of it before you administer the inscriptions with the non-profound tunnels.**
**And they are not called so simply because those do not stop the term of the bone from reaching to that which is near it, for this reason the tunnel is rounded extremity or margin on that which is left the head of it, resembling a margin or little circle, which prevents being submerged and passing through the thickness of the bone.**
**And it is convenient that you take many of these tunnels, each one fitting the particular shape of some bone, until you are present in all the tests of the skull, the edge of which is sharp, and the quantity in length and brevity is according to the quantity of the shape of this test.**
**And this is the form of three species of tunnels: The quality of perforating in the circuit of the broken bone is that you pause the tunnel on the bone and revolve it with those same words until you know that the bone is already penetrated; and then permit the tunnel to pass to another place, and pause there where it is between all the holes the quantity of the thickness of the ray or around it.**
**And then inscribe with inscriptions that are between each hole of the bone, and make it more subtle than you can on this side in the end of levitation, just as we have said, until you radiate the bone, or by your hand, or by some other cause for some instruments which you will have prepared to this, such as tweezers and forceps.**
**And it is necessary that you guard with all caution that the inscriber does not touch any cause of the ciphac.**
**And therefore, when you have perforated the bone with the tunnel, and it is separated from the ciphac if it continues to it, and you will have that extracted, it is necessary that you reason and equalize it in the roughness of it with another instrument similar to an inscriber, but more powerful and more subtle than the others.**
**And if there remains some small part of the bones, it is necessary that you take it with ease with the tools that are yours; and then cure the wound with linens and bandages which we have said.**
**And the other method of operation is light, distant from fear, which says Gualia and praises it greatly; and this is its sermon: necessary is to you at the beginning that you begin to discover the part of the bone at the place where the fracture is most violent and most manifest, until when you have discovered that part and have paused there with the end of this inscriber, slow and happy, which has this form:**
**And it is that the lenticular part is lion and does not inscribe any cause, and the acute part is two inches in length on either side before reaching the end of the bone, as times; that the lenticular part be adjusted to the ciphac with the face of the acute part in the bone.**
**And then strike with the inscriber on one side with a small hammer until you have inscribed all the bone with ease just as it is revolved, and you are sure of the padding that no accident will happen to you in any way, and if the medicant14 were the most foolish of all men and the most ignorant of their own; certainly, even if he were asleep.**
**And therefore, if there remains any cause annexed to the bone of the padding in some places of the bone, inscribe it with the end of the inscriber that is lenticular, and deliver it with ease, because it is delivered from its trouble and fear.**
**And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate into the padding, and what is abscessed or is left behind from the bone is the face of it, and remains in roughness and subtlety, then it is necessary that you smooth out that roughness and radiate those subtleties with razors subtle by which you have prepared the number, of various quantities so that it may be possible to administer those in every place the most convenient for them and the most right according to what has puzzled you your operation on that broken bone and its figure.**
**And it is necessary that you administer in your reason with which you sharpen the bone at the beginning with the most rough of those razors, and then use the most subtle one of them, and do not cease to do so according to continuity until you arrive at administering the most powerful and the most subtle of all.**
**But in any of the other small fractures, capillary and subtle fractures, it is necessary that you administer cure according to what has puzzled you for rectification of it.**
**And it is a cause that is not fully understood by all those who have studied in that art.** **And it is based on what we have shown in great fractures.**
**And if the padding is rectangular when you radiate the bone, then it is necessary that you take a cloth from it according to the quantity of the wound, and submerge it in rosy oil, and pause it over the orifice of the wound; and then take another cloth doubled or tripled and submerge it in vinegar and rosy oil, and pause it over the first cloth and make it as smooth as possible so that you do not injure the ciphac; and then administer a binding bandage over it, and do not tighten it except by the quantity of the wound as much as is necessary.**
**And leave it with this cure for one day or two until you are sure of a post-emptive caution; and then remove it and administer medicines with which excessive dryness is superfluous, such as razings of flax and farina of ears, and powder of senses and aristology, and similar things to those.**
**And it is that you should make a powder of these medicines which is powdered over the wound, just as they are dry; and universally, administer in that all medicine with properties of which one cleanses and does not bite.**
**And keep yourself according to your virtue that the wound in your cure be clean; and not be in a surdica of enguent or other; nor leave viral inflammation to arise there; for when it is adjusted over the padding of the skull, corrupts that and spoils that, and brings evil upon the patient from nearby malignant malice.**
**And evil occurs in the skull of the head, as if the bone is blackened and most especially when the cure is neglected, and there is darkness on the surface; and therefore consider now if evil befalls the patient with the accidents that we have said, know that it is pernicious for all doubt.**
**And if there is no blackness but from the medicine that is paused above, and it is in virtue of that medicine that makes that blackness, then you should take three parts of honey and three parts of rosy oil.** **And with those lines, make a cloth, and then pause it over the skull; and then cure that with the species of cure that is needed until it is healed.**
